O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, my very dear sons, I have completed for you this book which is the last of the science of medicine along with its completion, and have made the end through its expositions and its declarations. 
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete it for you with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, that is to say "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is neglected in our region and is altogether restricted, so the science is lost and diminished, and nothing remains of it except small descriptions in the books of the ancients that hands have copied.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come error and vanity, and understanding is obscured, and knowledge is distanced.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	Now it seems to me that I want to revive it along with the organization of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation;
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	and I will include along with it the forms of cautery irons, and other instruments of the work with the addition of the explanation and preparation of them, as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no good master of hands is found in our time, the art of medicine is diminished.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And whoever undertakes it must excel in the science of anatomy, as Galen said, so much that he knows the arrangement of the limbs, and their forms and connections and separations, and has knowledge of the bones and nerves and arms and their number, and the course of the moving and resting veins, and the location of their origin. 
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	And therefore Hippocrates said that the name with the name is much, and with the work is little; 
et meismement en l’art de main.	and especially in the art of the hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	We tell you in the introduction of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the aforementioned things, let him beware that he does not fall into error and kill people;
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	thus I have often seen several of those who undertake this science and so abandon themselves without knowledge and without experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	For I saw a foolish physician who cut an abscess of scrofula in the neck of a woman, and cut the arteries of the neck;
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	whereby so much blood came out that the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	And I saw another physician who removed a stone from an elderly man, and the stone was large;
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	he also removed with it a piece of the bladder, and the man was dead within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to remove it, and I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and I knew well that if he were cut, he would die from it.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	And I saw another physician who took into his care a duke of our land who had a broken leg, and along with the break there was a wound; 
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	and the physician, full of ignorance, tightened the break over the wound with splints, binding it very tightly, and did not leave any opening for the wound to drain, and left him like that for a period of time;
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	and ordered him not to untie it at all;
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	and it remained like that until the leg was completely swollen, and the foot as well, and it was ruined.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	I was called to come to him, and I hastened to come and untie the leg;
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	and when I had untied it, it was at peace and he felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	But nevertheless the infection was already established in the limb, and I could not heal it;
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	and the infection did not cease to spread through the limb until the limb was completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another physician who lanced a festering abscess, and then it inflamed due to the poor state of the patient's health. 
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a canker, when it is full of melancholic humor, should not be touched with iron unless it is in such a place that all that is corrupted can be removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	And therefore, dearest son, you need to know that manual work is divided into two parts:
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	namely, work where there is danger in several ways;
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	and I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	Therefore it is necessary that you protect yourself, so that foolish onlookers cannot speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	So take up your tools wisely, and treat your patients gently and firmly, and use the best method so that by the grace of God you will succeed and be praised;
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	and leave the frightening diseases of severe nature;
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	and remove yourself from that which makes you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can go from this world to the next in glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	Galen says in some of his admonishments:
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Do not undertake to treat a serious illness, lest you be called a foolish physician.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	 I have divided this treatise into three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	The first chapter is about fire cauteries and sharp medicinal cauteries, and the chapter is organized from the head to the feet;
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	and about the shapes of the instruments, and the cautery irons, and everything that is necessary for the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and cupping glasses, and wounds, and extracting arrows, and similar things;
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	and the chapter is organized with the shapes of the instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and sprains, and similar things;
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	and it is organized from the head down to the feet, and the shapes of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Before we recall the work, it is necessary that I describe the quality of help and the harm of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	I say that the qualities of help, and of harm, are the longest discourse and subtle science and the hidden secret;
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	and many wise men spoke of this, and agreed on it;
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	and their words suffice little for me, for I fear lengthiness.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	I say that cautery universally helps every complexion where there is matter, except for two complexions:
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	that is to say, a hot complexion without matter, and a dry complexion without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	In a complexion both hot and dry with matter, some debated and said that cautery is a great help there;
et li autre dirent le contraire:	and others said the opposite:
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	that cautery is not good for an illness that comes from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	For the nature of fire is hot, and a hot illness should not be treated with heat, nor with dryness;
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	and he who said the opposite claimed that cautery is a great help for a hot and dry illness that occurs in the bodies of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of a man and his moisture to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have sometimes found it through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	And in any case, no one should interfere except those who have experience, and who know through long practice the chapter on cauteries, and the diversity of human complexions, and the dispositions and causes of their illnesses, and the occurrences and the length of time;
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	We have no fear of other complexions, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the physicians assembled and agreed on the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that cautery with fire is among the secrets of healing, and of greater benefit than cautery with burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and does not go beyond the limb that is cauterized, and does not harm other limbs except a little.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	Burning medicines spread from limb to limb, and cause diseases in the limb that are difficult to heal;
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	and perhaps kill the patient.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Fire, because of its loftiness and the goodness of its substance, does not do this, unless there is excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	And this I have found for you through experiment and the length of service and study that I have put into the art, and it was based on the truth of things;
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	and for this I apologize for the length of the speech, for I do not want to deprive you of the secret that is contained in fire, and the quality of the work, how it expels diseases from bodies, as the philosopher says in demonstrating it;
or le recevez en vos pensees.	therefore receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on what time cauterizations should be done, and they chose spring.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	And I say that cautery is suitable in all seasons, because the sudden harm is lessened by the help of the cautery;
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	and especially if the cautery is for necessary, sudden, and urgent pains that cannot wait for the time when greater harm might come to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	And do not ever think, dear son, as the foolish physicians do;
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	for the illness that is healed by cautery does not return;
et il le dient ensi;	and they say it thus;
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	but it is not as they think, because cautery is only a medicine that changes the complexion, and dries the humors that are the cause of the pain, and is better than medicine because of the swiftness of its effect, and because of the power of its work and its mastery.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	And it is possible that the illness sometimes returns according to the complexion of the patient and the location of the illness and its nature;
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	and the superfluities are gathered in him by the intake of foods and similar things, unless cautery is administered in a place where there are few superfluities and moisture, such as cautery of teeth for pain, and similar things, and such pain does not return;
mais ce avient poc.	but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	And many people do not understand why cautery is called the last resort of medicine, and it is true;
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	but they do not believe that cautery is effective after medicine, but their understanding is false, and cautery is the last resort of medicine because when we administer methods of treatment for any disease and they are ineffective, then we administer cautery, and it is effective.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then it is clear that cautery is the last resort of medicine, not according to the understanding of foolish physicians.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	The ancients said that cautery with a gold instrument is gentler than with iron, and they only said this because of the quality of gold and the nobility of its substance; 
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	and they said that the site of the cautery does not suppurate, but this is not true because I have tested it, and I have found that it is true in some people; 
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	and gold cautery is better than iron, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	And yet when you heat a gold instrument, you do not know when it is hot because of the color of the gold, and it cools down quickly;
et s’on le chaufe trop;	and if it is heated too much;
si font au feu;	thus they make in the fire; 
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	and thus there is enough difficulty.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason we use iron cauteries that we have prepared specifically for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Now I have organized this chapter from head to toe so that the way is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	of the olive-shaped cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is good for moisture and coldness on the brain, and there are two that are made for a disease called "soda," and for many humors that descend from the head to the eyes, and to the ears, and for excessive dreams and toothache and sore throat, and especially for all illnesses that come from coldness like paralysis and lethargy and apoplexy and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	The method for this cautery is that the patient be purged by a laxative medicine cleansing the head for three or four nights, depending on what the strength and age and constitution of the patient can tolerate;
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	and then shave the patient's head.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	And then have him sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on his chest;
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	then place the base of your palm on the bridge of his nose between his two eyes;
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	and there where your middle finger falls, bleed from the vein then heat the cautery which is called "olivare," of which this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	And place it on the spot marked with ink, and do so while pressing down and tightening your hand little by little while twisting;
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	then lift your hand quickly and look at the spot to see if you can see the bone just a little;
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	and if you do not see it, repeat the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you;
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	afterwards take a little salt and put it in water and soak cotton in it, and place it on the spot, and leave it for three days;
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	afterwards apply cotton soaked in butter;
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	and leave it on until the burn is gone;
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	afterwards treat the wound with the ointment called "tetrapharmacon", until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	And the ancients said that the longer the wound remains open, the more it is cleansed;
et por ce si aide mues.	and therefore it heals better/faster. (or "therefore, it promotes healing")
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And some of these said that one should leave the cautery on until part of the bone is burned, and then one cuts away what is burned from the bone, and it is treated/healed.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	And others say that one should leave the cautery on, and push so strongly that one lowers/scoops out the bone as wide as a whorl that women put on their spindles so that the humors come out better/faster;
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	and one should leave the wound open for a long time;
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	afterwards one should treat and solder/close it.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	And these two methods of cautery do not seem to me to be good at all, except in some men where there is cause for fear;
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	and it seems better to me that I should leave it;
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	for the head (of the bone) is weakened by the continuous discharges of (bodily) fluids, as we observe in other limbs;
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	and also when the patient's head (of the bone) is naturally weak, and the first type of cautery is safer and better for me, and this one I use with the work together for healing.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the chronic pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	When chronic pain occurs throughout the head, and lasts a long time, the patient should use irises and pills which are called "cochie," and purging of the head and oils and plasters;
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	and if the cautery that we mentioned earlier is performed, and it is not effective.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	Take care if the patient's head (constitution) is of a strong nature, and that it is not too cold;
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	then cauterize it a little below the cautery that we mentioned above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	Afterwards, make a cautery on each temple of the head down to the bone, as we have said before, and make a cautery in the place that is called "temples/vessels";
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	and it is a place where one puts cupping glasses;
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	and lighten your hand so that you do not go down to the bone:
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	the patient feels much greater pain in this cautery than in the others, and I will speak of it elsewhere;
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	and it is necessary that the cauteries of the temples be more subtle/smaller/shallower than those with which one cauterizes the middle of the head, and this is the method/form:
dou cautere dou chief	of the cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	When in a part of the head comes a sudden pain, and the ailment extends to the eye, and the head is purged by cleansing medicines, and one has done the other treatments that I have described in the section on illnesses, and all this is of no use:
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	then make cauteries in two ways, that is to say, with a sharp medicine and with iron.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	The cautery with sharp medicine is that you take a clove of garlic, and remove the skin and cut off a little at both ends, and then split the temple where the pain is located in such a way that you can place the clove of garlic under the skin;
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	and when it is placed, bind it and hold it firmly and leave it thus for twelve hours;
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	and then unbind it and take out the clove of garlic, and leave the wound like that for two or three days;
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	then put on cotton dipped in butter until pus comes out.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	Afterwards treat it with ointment until it is healed;
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	and if you wish, do this with some burning medicines that I have written about in the twelfth treatise on burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is done in this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery, which has this shape:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	And it is called "closed" because the head is shaped like a nail or has a slight curve, and in the middle has a small point;
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	and place it on the painful spot, and hold your hand steady and turn the iron slightly, so that half the thickness of the skin is burned;
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	and lift your hand so that the artery, which is outside, is not burned, and a lot of blood flows out.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;	Afterwards, put cotton in salt water and place it on the spot for three days;
puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	then put cotton soaked in butter, and then treat the area with ointment until it is healed;
et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	and if you want to cauterize this migraine with the cautery which is called "cultellare," use the very tip, and be careful not to cut the artery in this migraine which is not old.
de emigraine	of migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	When you treat a migraine as we have said before in the divisions of illnesses, and it is not effective, and you see that the previously mentioned cauterizations with medicine and iron are not sufficient, then it is necessary that you heat the cautery which is called "cultellare" until it is white;
et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	and thus mark on the painful area a line half a finger long, and remove your hand immediately, and take care not to cut the artery and that you do not reach the bone;
et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	and beware of the mandible that moves when one chews, and be mindful of the nerve that moves it so that spasm does not come to the patient, and beware of bleeding from the artery when it is cut, where cutting brings great fear, especially to him who does not know it, and who is not a student and experienced;
et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;	and leave the work halfway done;
mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	but I will tell you how to stop the bleeding when the artery is cut, and I will show you the place where it is appropriate in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And if you see that this cautery is not enough for the illness, and the patient is suffering, cauterize him in the middle of the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed;
et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;	and if you wish, administer the cautery that we mentioned in the chapter on the extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has two blades;
et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	and this cautery is better than that one and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of ear pain from cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When ear pain comes from cold, and one has used dissolving medicines and other treatments that we have mentioned in the section, and the pain does not change, then heat this cautery which is called "points," of which here is the form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche;	Afterward, prick all around the affected ear, or around both if the pain is in both, and move a little above the base of the ear after you have marked the place with ink;
et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;	and make ten points around each ear;
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	afterward treat the area until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	Torture that must be treated by cautery is excluded except for those that arise from phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of illnesses;
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	and do not cauterize similar conditions that come from dryness and nerve spasms.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:	When you treat this type of torture that arises from phlegm with hydragogues and purges of the head and gargles, and this is not effective, then you must cauterize the patient with three cauteries:
l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	one at the root of the ear, and another a little outside the temple, and the third at the joining of the two lips;
et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;	and place the cautery on the part that appears healthy, and make a cautery near the top of the ear, a little below the crown of the head, and another on the temple about a thumb's length long;
et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;	and leave the cautery in place until half of the core is burned;
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the shape of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;	And it is similar to the lancet that we have shown before, but it is a little more subtle, and the blade should be a little thicker;
aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	afterwards treat the area as I have said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:	When apoplexy is long-standing and you treat it as we have said, and it does not help, and the patient does not have a fever, then make four cauteries:
II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;	Two on the two temples of the head, and one in the middle of the head, and one in the place called "vessels" as we have said before, and the last cautery on the pit of the stomach;
et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	and be treated as we have said before.
de litargie	of lethargy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil;	For this illness, it is necessary to give the patient strong herbs and pills that cleanse the brain;
aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres;	afterwards, shave the patient's entire head, and apply to the occiput the mustard plaster that is described in the treatise on plasters;
et c’est li maniere dou cautere:	and this is the method of cautery:
si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est;	If he is healed thus, it is good;
et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros;	and if he is not, then make three cauteries down the middle of the head, descending to the neck, and let the space between each cautery be the width of a thumb;
et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu;	and treat it like the others, and if you wish to add more, and the patient is tolerant, make a cautery in the middle;
et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if necessary, two others on the two temples, and treat him until he is healed;
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	and let the cautery be the one called "olivary," as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of the coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit;	It is necessary that the head be cleansed of air and of what we have said before;
aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col;	afterwards shave the patient's head, then cauterize him in the middle of the head and on each temple, and one behind and three on the spine of the neck;
et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos;	and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient is tolerant, and the illness is strong, make four cauteries on the spine of the back;
et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main;	and leave them until the thickest part of the wound is burned, and lift your hand;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	afterwards treat it until it is healed, and let the cautery, which is called "olivary," be as we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	Of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptic should not use cautery except for one who is phlegmatic, and it is necessary to first purify the brain with herbs and other treatments that we have mentioned in the section when the patient is old enough and able to take medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;	And if it is a child who cannot tolerate it, have them gargle and chew things that purify the brain often, along with good foods;
aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;	afterwards shave the head in the middle, and make a cautery there according to what we have said before, and a cautery on the forehead, and on each temple;
et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and if the patient is strong and able to bear it, cauterize them as I have said for one who has paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to the method I have described.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, make a small cautery in this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When, due to melancholy, the superfluities or humors are corrupted and the phlegm is thick, then cauterize them with such cauteries as we have described for one who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if, due to melancholy, the superfluity is tending towards melancholy, and the patient's body is moist, then give him to drink something by which the brain may be cleansed, according to what is stated before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide;	Afterward, shave the patient's head;
aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief;	then make a compress of well-made linen, like a circle, and place it in the middle of the head;
et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars;	and let the patient sit cross-legged and be well supported on all sides;
aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien;	then present the ointment, and aged sheep butter is good;
et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;	and warm it moderately over a fire, so that the finger can tolerate it if placed within;
aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;	then empty the circle in the middle of the head, and let it cool;
et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and do this to the patient once a week with other good management, until he is healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or if you want to cauterize it by making multiple points with the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument;	This method of cautery softens the brain evenly;
et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	and then apply cotton soaked in butter and chicken fat.
de l’awe des eulz	of the water of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When water first comes to the eyes, by the signs I have mentioned in the division, then begin by giving the patient a drink that cleanses the head, and protect him from all moisture, and make him sweat in a bath several times while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I;	Afterwards, tell him to shave his head, and make a cautery in the middle of the head, and make two cauteries on both temples if the flow of water is in both eyes together, or in one if the flow is in one eye;
et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple;	and cut with the cautery all the veins and arteries that are under the skin, and let the cauteries be long according to the width of the temple;
et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	and beware of excessive bleeding, and if you see too much blood coming out, stop it with such power as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras;	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and at the incision the precaution of how you will stop it;
et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	and sometimes one makes a cautery or cauterization under the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	of the body of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors;	When the tears of the eyes are old and habitual and are on the veins, or next to the arteries that are in the visible part of the head;
et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz:	and one sees that it is from cold phlegmatic superfluities, then make for him the cautery that I spoke of at the beginning of the water descending to the eyes:
I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os;	One cautery in the middle of the head, and two cauteries on the two temples, and two cauteries or cauterizations under the two bones;
et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	and if there is need for more, then cauterize him carefully above the eyebrow with a small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	of the body of tears from within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies;	When you treat it according to what we have said in the division, and it does not help, then give the patient three nights of cochies (a sort of medicinal drink) to drink;
aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire;	afterwards shave the head and apply a cautery in the middle of the olive-shaped cautery mark;
et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous;	and make two cauteries with the cautery called "clavilis" above the two eyebrows, slightly below the hairline;
et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	and beware of the artery so that you do not cut it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the shape of the cautery that is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the eyelid is softened by illness and moisture, then cauterize it with this cautery which is called "olivare." (olive-shaped)
de coi ci est li forme:	of which here is the shape:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont;	And if you wish, make two cauteries on the two eyebrows, as long as the eyebrows are;
et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and do not remove the hand except when the third part of the eyelid is burned, in the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	of the hair that pricks the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	Sometimes it happens that the eyelashes are turned inwards, and prick the eye, and cauteries are made there in two ways:
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	that is to say with fire, or with burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals;	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even;
et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain;	When they grow and are even, then place the patient in your lap;
aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz;	then draw on the eyelid a figure like a myrtle leaf, and let the beginning of the mark be near the hairs;
puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	then place cotton moistened with egg white and psyllium mucilage on the eye, then heat the cautery, which has this shape:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit;	Then cauterize over the figure you have marked little by little, many times, so that the flesh is burned there;
et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;	and the sign of the success of the operation is that you see the eyelid retracted and the hairs raised at the corner of the eye;
adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	then remove your hand, and leave it thus for three days, then put cotton soaked in butter there until the burn is healed;
aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	afterwards treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers;	And if after this the hairs return and the eyelid is softened, then repeat the cautery over the same spot, as you did the first time;
et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	and if the hairs are burned away, cauterize it until the eyelid is raised to its natural position and is even, and the hairs do not prick the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte;	The cautery of burning medicine is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even, then make from parchment the shape of a myrtle leaf;
puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien;	then take French soap and quicklime, an ounce of each, and grind them well together;
et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz;	and do it quickly, so that it does not cool, then spread it on the shape you have made like the myrtle leaf, and place it on the eyelid;
et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi;	And if the patient has it in one eye only, you should work on one, and if in both, also;
et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef;	and place under the eye cotton moistened in egg white;
et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	and the patient's head should be in your lap and put your index finger on the medicine, and press it a little and move it every time the patient feels a burning from the medicine, for it feels like a burning fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, remove the medicine with your finger.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision;	And when the burning has passed, lift up the moistened area and see if you notice the growth elevated as if it had been raised by the use of fire or by an incision;
et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	and if it is so, it is good.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point;	If not, then apply more medicine to the area where the medicine has not worked, until your work is even, and your mark is precise;
puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then apply cotton moistened with butter until the burned area falls off, afterward treat the area with the ointment called "dyafenis" and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And you must take great care in your work, ensuring that none of the medicine falls into the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;	And if the paper softens afterward, and the hairs prick the eye, then reapply the medicine to the softened area of the paper neatly, just as you did before;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	afterward treat it until it is healed;
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	and this is the shape of the myrtle leaf:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	And know that people's eyes vary in size, and your restraints should be adjusted accordingly;
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	and the right way is not set forth for the one who studies this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	of the treatment of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have described in the divisions of diseases, and your treatments are not effective, then you must apply cautery in this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	Instruct the patient to put their head in your lap; 
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	and let the assistant hold their head between their hands in such a way that they cannot move or shake their head;
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	then place cotton moistened in egg white or parsley juice over the eye;
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	then heat the cautery, which is like this:
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	and it is shaped at the tip like a feather of a vulture, together as one the cautery should be;
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	if you wish, it can be pointed from one end to the other, and if you wish, it can be like a tent;
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	but still, this one that is pointed is better for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	Then press the fistula if it is open, and draw out the pus, and dry it;
et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;	and if it is closed, then open it, and draw out the matter;
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;	then apply the cautery hot, and hold your hand to the cautery on the side of the nose above the eye, so that your hand doesn't cause harm;
et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	and place the cautery in the fat of the eye, and destroy it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you reach the bone at the beginning of the cauterization, that would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	If not, repeat the cauterization again, and again if you need to, and leave it for three days;
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;	afterwards apply cotton soaked in butter, and treat it with the drying ointment until it is healed, and if forty days pass and it is not healed, then apply a sharp corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed;
et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	and then treat it according to what is appropriate in its chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a method of cauterization for fistula that some of the ancients described.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;	Attend to the fistula, and cut open the area;
aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	afterwards place in the incision a thin tube, of which here is the form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;	and they make it about the size of a third of a lead weight;
et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;	and hold your hand or the tube firmly, and let the patient not move at all, so that the melted lead does not run into his eye;
et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:	and it is necessary to put on the patient's eye cotton moistened in egg white or in water:
li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	the lead thus burns the site of the fistula, and heals it by marvelous healing.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have described, that is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, it is necessary to administer a perforation to the nerve, and bring back the fistula to the body of the nerve as appropriate in its proper place.
des crevaices en levres	of cracks in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Very often cracks occur in the lips that are called "poil," and especially in the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks with what we have described in divisions, and the treatment is not effective, then heat a small knife-shaped cautery in this way:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font;	And quickly put it in those cracks until it reaches the bottom;
aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	afterwards treat the area with cerate until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;	When an abscess comes at the base of the throat or in the uvula, or in the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, afterwards it causes rotting and pus and becomes chronic and becomes a fistula;
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:	and you treat it as we have described in divisions, and it is not effective:
adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;	then you must have a cautery according to the size of the fistula;
aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu;	after the opening or hole of the fistula, and hold your hand steady so that the hot iron reaches the bottom of it, and to the furthest point;
et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do this once or twice, then treat it with what we have described in treatments, until it is healed;
et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin;	and if it is healed thus, that is good;
et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	and if not, then it is necessary to uncover the place and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	of the movement of teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth are loose, and you treat them with medicines and it is of no use, then place the patient's head in your lap;
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;	afterwards, heat the cautery, the shape of which will come later, in such a way that you place a small chain on the tooth;
et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;	and place the hot cautery inside quickly, and hold your hand there so that the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth;
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;	afterwards, remove your hand and reapply the cautery as you wish;
aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	afterwards, have the patient fill their mouth with salt water, and hold it for an hour and then spit it out.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way the tooth that was loose is strengthened, and the softened gums are tightened, and the corrupted moisture is dried.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	When toothache comes from cold, or there is cold or a worm, and medical treatments are ineffective, then cautery is necessary in two ways:
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	and cautery with butter and cautery with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	Cautery with butter is as follows: you take cow's butter and melt it in an iron or bronze spoon;
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	then take cotton and wrap it around the tip of a tent, and soak it in boiling butter, and quickly place it on the aching tooth and hold it there until it cools;
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	and do this often until its virtue reaches the root of the tooth, and if you wish, soak wool and cotton in cold butter, and place it on the aching tooth, and place a hot iron on it until the heat reaches the end of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	The cautery with combined fire is as follows: you take a tube of iron or bronze, and it should be thick so that the fire does not reach the patient's mouth;
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	then heat the cautery, the shape of which will come later, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand there until the cautery cools;
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	do this often, for the pain will be removed that same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	And the patient should fill his mouth with good butter immediately after this cautery, and then spit it out;
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the shape of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;	And make a cautery of whichever end you want, and according to what you are able to do;
et c’est li forme de la caine:	and this is the form of the tube:
des scrophules	of scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;	When scrofula is caused by phlegm and cold humors, and does not respond to digestion by medicines, then heat the pointed cautery, of which the form follows below, and it should have two openings for the fumes to escape from the cautery on the other side;
et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume;	and place the hot cautery on the abscess once, or twice if necessary, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess;
et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors;	and if the abscess is small, apply the cautery according to the size of the abscess, and leave it thus for three days;
et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee;	and apply cotton soaked in butter until the burn is gone;
aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	afterwards treat the area with ointments and tents until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The shape of the dog:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives;	When the humors prevail over the bronchial tubes of the lung, and especially when this comes from a cold complexion, then the patient must first be purged by laxative medicines;
aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	afterwards make a cautery at the base of the throat, and be careful not to go down as far as the throat, and do not burn the heart but only a little.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant;	Then make another cautery at the joint of the neck at the top of the spine, and let the cautery be what is called "clavile" of which we have the image before;
et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat the place as we have said before until it is healed.
de la toust	of the cough
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai .II cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis;	When the cough and lung disease are from cold humors, and the patient has no fever or dryness, and the illness is chronic, make two cauteries on the chest in empty places;
et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles;	and another cautery in the middle of the chest between the two breasts;
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	and let the cautery, which is called "clavile," be according to the form described previously.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles;	And if you wish, make a cautery by pricking, with the cautery called "points," the form of which is described above in the section on ear diseases;
et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	and let the pricks be up to thirty, or thereabouts.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	Afterwards, treat the area as described previously, and let the cautery have three prongs according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And for this reason, the cauteries are easier because you make three at a time.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	On the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit;	Afterwards, have the patient lie on his back and on his side;
aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre;	After, lift the core that is inside the areola with the fingers of your left hand;
et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	And if the joint is dislocated inwards, then heat the cautery which has two nerves, of which here is the shape:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres;	and cauterize the core until it pierces through to the rib, and the shape of the cautery would come to resemble four cauteries;
et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres;	and for this reason, cauterization is done with the cautery that has three nerves, which is why the shapes of the cauterization are six cauteries;
et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and the nerves are as thin as a probe and this is the shape of the cautery which has three nerves:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And sometimes another nerve is added to this, which makes eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil;	Afterward, apply crushed leeks with salt onto the cautery;
aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	afterwards, let the patient rest, and the limb should not be moved for a long time until it is well strengthened.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated from above, which rarely happens, then cauterize on the thick part of the clavicle cautery, with many cauterizations by pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and the moisture is removed, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When coldness and much moisture enter the stomach, so much so that they alter its complexion, and catarrh increases in it, and the usual methods of treatment are used and they are not effective, then the patient must be laid on his back, and extend his legs and arms.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture;	After this, make three cauterizations: one below the hollow of the chest by the width of a finger, with the clavicle cautery, and two cauterizations outside on both sides, so that the shape of the cauterizations forms a triangle, and there is enough space between them so that they do not join together when they expel pus; 
et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	and let the cauterizations be so deep that they penetrate the two parts of the heart, and let the shape of the cauterizations be according to this form without adjustment:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme;	And if you wish to cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this form;
et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche;	and he who is afraid of this cautery, should cauterize by pricking and mark a point on the stomach according to the amount of ink you want;
puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	then cauterize it with the cautery which is called "point.
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the ailment that we have discussed before, until he is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez;	When pain comes to the liver from cold and moisture and from great flatulence, so much so that it is forced out of its natural complexion by the superfluities;
et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil;	and the patient is treated with what we have said in divisions, and it does not benefit him, so it is necessary that the patient be laid on his back;
et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient;	and mark three cauteries according to this form and this figure and this quantity over the liver, below the hypochondria, there where the man's elbow reaches;
et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi;	and have a space between each cautery the width of a finger;
et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere;	and let the cauteries be along the length of the body, and do not press your hand very hard with the whole cautery;
et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez;	and only burn half of the core, and let the patient stand upright on his feet;
et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais;	and if he cannot, then he should lie down, and extend his legs, and raise his arms;
et c’est li forme:	and this is the method:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors;	And if you wish, cauterize these cauteries with a knife, if you are skillful and wise in the art, and be careful not to burn the whole core, for you would dry out the whole body;
et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	and do not let it come to a boil, for the core is very delicate there, and know this for certain.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile:	When there is an abscess on the liver, and you want to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane:
s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort;	if it is in the flesh, the patient feels a pain, not too strong;
et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	and if it is in the membrane, he feels a raging pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste;	And then when this treatment requires the eyes, it is necessary that the patient be supported on his head;
et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	and then mark with ink the place where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which is similar to a spoke, of which here is the form:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers;	And cauterize with the cautery until the core is burned, and goes down to the syphac, until all the pus is out;
aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez;	after treat it according to the treatment for issues until it is healed;
et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	and no one should use this cautery except someone who has studied long in the art of medicine, and through whose hands these diseases have passed sometime.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then he can work boldly, and yet it seems to me that it is better to leave it alone. 
dou cautere de pleuresin	Of the cautery of pleurisy
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere:	The ancients said that for pleurisy, cauteries should be made from the roots of birthwort, and in this manner:
pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois;	Take a long birthwort root, the largest you can find, and let it be dry, and be as thick and as long as your finger;
et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe;	and soak it in oil, and light it on fire, and cauterize one cautery between the armpit and the neck, and two small cauteries a little lower down in the area that is below the chin;
et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc;	and two cauteries between the fifth rib and the sixth, sloping downwards a little;
et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules;	and one cautery in the middle of the chest, and another over the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and two on the two sides of the chest outside the cautery that is between the two shoulders;
et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	and do not press your hand, but do it lightly as if smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme;	And some ancients said that some men use an iron cautery resembling a razor, and heat it and place it between the ribs, until it reaches that abscess;
