Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and from what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by throwing stones, and cutting with a sword and knife, or with a lance or wood or arrow, or similar things;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or that they are made according to the places of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the chest, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the treatment for each wound, and will begin with the simple wounds of the head, for the complex one will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut:	I say that when a simple wound occurs on the head, and the bone is not broken, take note if it is from a thrown stone or similar things, and the skin is nevertheless broken and the wound is large, and you suspect the development of a hot abscess:
si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	then immediately have them bleed from the cephalic vein, especially if little blood comes from the wound, and let the bleeding be on the opposite side of the injured part;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and the patient should avoid excess of wine and rich foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if they do not want to be bled, then let their food be light, and let them not drink wine, nor eat meat;
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put on the wound, if a hot abscess develops there, cotton soaked only in rose oil, or in styptic wine;
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no hot abscess, then put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood and has not been exposed to the air, a powder, which I will describe a little later;
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the burn has altered it, then apply some ointments until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like from a sword cut or similar, and the edges cannot be brought together by tents, then join them by stitching, as I will describe for wounds of the belly, concerning stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope;	If the wound exposes bone and hangs, attached only slightly, cut it off;
puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat rich foods, such as head cheese and cooked wheat, also like chicken, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find rot in the skin, and it does not reach the bone, cut away all the rot, and throw it away, then treat it;
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	And if there is an artery or vein in the wound from which blood flows, and it cannot be stopped with medicines, then search for the artery, and if you find it displaced, tie it with a thread;
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if that doesn't work, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere:	And if these wounds are small and simple, the treatment is easy:
et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	and put in this powder which heals before the burn changes it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est:	And the composition of the powder is:
pren encens une partie;	take one part incense;
sanc de dragon II parties;	two parts dragon's blood;
chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	three parts quicklime, and powder it finely, and fill the wound, and bind it tightly, until it heals well and joins with all its blood;
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle;	and then tie it well, and leave it unbound unless it swells;
car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	for the medicine is not removed until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes this is done with lime alone, when one does not have the incense or the dragon's blood, but the burn must not have changed the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the burn has changed the wound, especially in summer, then this powder is not applied;
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but apply some digestive ointments, or a poultice of barley flour made with water and honey, until it suppurates;
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if a bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with fine forceps; 
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you later about fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound occurs in the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the nerve, there is no other method than to leave it to heal, and not put anything restrictive on it, because it harms the nerves and makes them retract;
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not put anything cold on the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and their connection is with the brain, which is the highest member;
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	but the medicine should be soft, such as warm water washed in fresh water, and mixed with rose oil, and cuckoo pint also washed in fresh water, and other mineral stones in this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then sew it and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and it is filled with pus and mud, then pierce it in the lowest place;
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	And if the artery is cut, and bleeding occurs, then uncover it, and wash it, and cauterize it if necessary;
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	And if the windpipe of the throat is cut, or the heart, and the tube is preserved, through which the food passes, then sew the heart over the tube of the throat, and do not touch the throat but put it back according to its natural shape;
et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	And then bind it conveniently, and leave it for some days, then treat it with drying ointments until it is healed;
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	And if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then scrape it;
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	And if there are pieces of bone, then pull them all out if you can, and those that you cannot get, leave them until the wound festers, and is opened and the passage cleared;
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wound is fresh, then sprinkle on the powder that I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is a fistula, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound of a lance or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:	If it is a blow from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, then see if air escapes from the wound when the patient breathes:
saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	know then that the wound is mortal;
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put the powder in it at the first hour, nor bind it because of the blood so that it does not remain deep inside and return to the heart, and kill the patient;
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor;	but put on a drawing ointment, and bind it twice a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;	and if you have no ointment, put old cotton in the wound to suck out the moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more;
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;	thus no spasm will come, nor trembling sickness of the heart, nor shortness of breath;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see good signs, know that the wound is safe.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat it with tents and other treatments until it is healed;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;	and if it cannot heal, and festers, then know that there is a fistula;
si la cure si com on doit.	so treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a sword cut or knife, and it is simple, whether on the chest or the back, treat it as described previously;
s’elle est grans, de cousture;	if it is large, with sutures;
et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	and if it is small, with powder, and if it is pressed into the bone, and has broken off pieces, then explore the wound, and draw them out if they are detached;
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not detached, let the wound fester, so the extraction will be easier;
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and the judgment for other wounds in other limbs is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly/abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The rupture of the belly/abdomen is large and medium and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	from the large wound sometimes the intestine, or the sinews of the intestines, protrude, making their insertion difficult;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	and the stitching is more difficult, and sometimes the small wound is worse than the large one, because it is more difficult to put the intestines back in unless one replaces them promptly;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	because the intestines swell as soon as they feel the cold, thus making them more difficult to replace, and therefore the medium wound is better, because the intestine is more easily returned to its place than in the other two.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	And know that the rupture of the abdomen/belly occurs in four ways:
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	the two common sutures occur in the suturing of the abdomen/belly, and the suturing of other wounds of the body and two other specific sutures are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and yet they are more specific with the suturing of the abdomen/belly, and I will describe and explain each one.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	I say that when the wound is small, and some part of the intestine comes out, and it is difficult to put back, this is because of one of the two ways:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen from the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it in this way:
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	wet a sponge or a soft cloth in lukewarm water only, or in which you cook squinant, cypress, and spikenard in water, and sprinkle the intestine until the swelling is gone;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and sometimes make this wine astringent, and it is better than plain water for reducing swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	And when you see the swelling subside, then moisten the intestine with water in which marshmallow and mallow have been cooked, for by this the opening is soothed a little;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then cut the wound a little with the instrument with which one cuts hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	and the first treatment is better than cutting, for no one should cut there unless there is great necessity;
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and this is the instrument for cutting it:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	cut inside the curve and not outside, and see here the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine protrudes, put it back according to its natural form in its proper place, if you are able, for that is much better.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	When the wound is large, and it is in the lower part of the belly, you must make the patient lie on his back, and place his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	and if it is in the lower part of the belly, put the head and chest higher than the lower parts, and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts, take care that the injured part is higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus one must manage what I say for large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	In small wounds, apply what is prepared for you, then have at hand a compassionate assistant who holds the entire rupture in his hand, and brings the edges together;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	and this is the common method of stitching, and it is that you take a needle or several, depending on the width of the wound, then leave a finger's width of space from the top of the wound, and insert a needle there with a good strong thread;
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	and pierce both edges of the skin along with both edges of the siphac, which is under the skin inside, until you make it pierce through to the other side, and bring the two edges of the siphac, all four together;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	then tie it with a double thread around the needle on both sides, then bring the two edges of the wound together neatly, then leave a finger's width of space, and insert another needle there;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	then tie it with the thread as you did the first needle, and continue doing this according to how many needles you need, until the entire wound is closed;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	and the needles should be medium, between fine and thick, because fine needles cut through all the flesh, and those that are too thick cannot enter well:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	therefore they must be medium-sized;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	and the needles should not be placed too deep in the flesh and skin, so that they don't cut and open the wound before it heals;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and then cut off the heads of the needles, so they do not injure the patient while sleeping, and place tents or cloths at the ends of the needles to hold them still, and leave them until the wound is healed;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	and this method of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds, because one or two needles are sufficient.
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	The second stitch is common, and is that you bring the two edges of the skin and the two edges of the muscle together with a needle threaded with a strong, medium-sized thread;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	and when you have pierced all four of these edges together, bring the needle back to the side where you began, in the way that cloth is sewn;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and leave a space between each stitch the width of a little finger;
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	this stitch is common knowledge, and I sewed a wound that a man had in his belly, who was wounded with a knife, and the wound was more than a handspan long, and his intestines were protruding a good two handspans, and the wound was in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I put his intestines back in after they had been out for twenty-four hours, and the wound was stitched up within fifteen days, and I treated him, and he was healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the physicians had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not treat him with ointment, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicines;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I simply put old cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle, and push it from the outside part to the inside;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	when it has pierced the center straight through, then take the end of the thread or suture where you pushed the needle, and make it pierce on the other side from inside to outside;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and the meaning of this stitch is that you sew as leatherworkers do hides, and that you leave the thread once on one side, and take it again on the other, until the stitching is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second way of stitching, which Galen specifically describes, is like some do, who bring the two parts together naturally, and join one end of the thread to the other end, in this manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	insert a needle at the end of the wound nearby, and make it pierce only that spot, and leave the two ends of the thread;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	then turn the needle and make it pierce from the outside to the inside, at the two ends of the thread;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then make it pierce both from the outside to the inside, at two other ends of the wound that are on the other side;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the best way of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	Galen said these words, and some testify to it, that one should sew the belly with two needles, where there is thread in each one;
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one should push one needle from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew leather straps;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, then the stitching is more difficult than in other places of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The treatment of the wound is like the treatment of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, before the air has changed it, so replace the intestine, and sew it;
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	then put on the powder generating flesh, and if the air has changed it, then put on some ointment that is available, until the wound swells;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and one hundred threads, and the superficial tissues should be joined, and the peritoneum;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the wound like the others, until it is healed;
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and if you have no medicines, so put on, as soon as it begins to swell, old cotton, and change it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you do not need other medicine in most cases when the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and if you are worried that the wound will spread to the principal members, then you must soak light wool in oil of moderate heat, or in rose oil, and place it around the groin, and under the armpits;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	and if he feels pain or pus in the bowels, and it often happens, then give enemas of lukewarm dark wine, especially if the pus comes down to the intestine; 
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and it pierces within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine which is called "jejunum" cannot heal when it is wounded, and this is because of the arrangement of the veins that are there, and because of the delicateness of the whole body, and the closeness of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the omentum protrudes from the wound, put it back in just like the intestine, while it is fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	and if it is old and has become green or black, you must tie off the place that is black, so that bleeding does not occur there, because there are veins and arteries;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	then cut what is between the two ligatures, and let the two ends hang from the part below the wound down outside to ease the extraction when the omentum falls off, and the wound closes.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the scrotum
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	When the intestine is round, and the wound is small, it can be repaired in some men, because I saw that a man was wounded in the belly by a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and the wound was to the right of the stomach, and it festered and became a fistula, and the excrement and gas came out of it;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I treated it as best I could, and did not stop refining the treatment until he was healed, and the place closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it closed, I feared that the patient would have pain in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and he had no pain, but remained in better condition, eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and some experimenters said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, that it must be tied up in this manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	Take wheat grains with large heads, then bring the lips of the wound together, and when the wheat grain has opened its mouth, place it on the two lips so that it tightens its mouth over them;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	and then cut off the head, and it holds so that it cannot come undone, then put another wheat grain next to it in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely enclosed;
et cout la plaie.	and sew the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	These heads then dry up in the intestine, and no harm comes to the patient, and one can tie the intestine with a fine thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal, in this manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	take the end of this intestinal thread that is very thin, and then tie a thin twisted linen thread to the end of this thread, then put the thread in the needle, and sew the intestine with it, and bring it back into the rupture;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this method of stitching with wheat grains is only according to the way of trust and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the small intestines, there is no remedy or healing, except subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it becomes chronic, is universally called a "fistula", and especially when it is deep and produces pus.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	And a fistula, in truth, is a false, hard, white knot, where there is no feeling of pain, and is as deep as the feather of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes it discharges clear pus, and other times thick;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes little, and other times a lot;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	and I have already spoken of it in the division of wounds, that any wound that is not healed, and where there is no flesh, is only due to one of nine causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	namely, because of lack of blood or bodily strength;
ou por sa malice;	or because of its malignancy;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard flesh inside, and on the edges, which prevents new flesh from growing;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or there is too much pus;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or the place is rotten, and the matter is of poor quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or the medicine is not good for the treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the infection is like a pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because of the characteristics of the region, digestion is slow, and healing is slow, and it swells naturally;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	or there are veins or bones there:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the medical treatments in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now I must inform you about the treatment of a fistula that is made by hand. (surgically created)
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that a fistula can occur in all parts of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	for there are fistulas that occur in the large veins, and in the arteries, and in the nerves, or in the peritoneum, or in the intestine, or in the bladder, or in some of the ribs, or in the spine of the back, or in any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and there are some that occur in the principal member itself, and in similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all fistulas of this kind are difficult to heal, and there is nothing but work and ignorance (involved in treating them); 
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if there is a fistula that does not reach the place that I have mentioned, and you are confident in the treatment, and you want to examine it, then take a probe of brass or iron, if the fistula is straight, and explore it;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	and if the fistula is crooked, then search it with a thin lead probe, for lead bends easily around the crookedness;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot probe it well, then irrigate it through one of the openings, for the moisture will run from one opening to another and cleanse it;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	then explore it carefully as best you can, so that you know if there is bone or nerve involved, and its depth, and ask the patient carefully about the pain he feels from the pressure of your hand, and the place where he feels it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and when you truly know the location where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, then cut it according to what I have told you, and remove entirely the corrupted matter and flesh that are within;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	and then treat it until it is healed, and if the fistula is very deep in a straight line, then you must cut deeply, as much as you can, then put in tents soaked in a sharp medicine, and push them right to the end of the fistula, so that the medicine corrodes the excess that remains at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then put in ointments that generate healthy flesh, until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerve does not hinder you in the principal members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, then scrape it until the corruption is all removed, then treat it with things that generate flesh until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	and if it is not healed, and returns to pus as before, know that you have not gone deep enough:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	so uncover and search until you are at the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore the place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healed, that is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too deep, that you cannot reach it;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	so there is no other solution than to leave it to nature;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there is a small corrupted bone, and you can pull it with forceps, extract it with a suitable instrument, and if there are many bones, pull them all out, do not leave a single one;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	and if the moisture hinders you, and there is no error or fear, cut both moisture and flesh, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	And if you cannot remove them at once, apply something generating rot to the wound, and leave it until the place is rotted around the bones, and then they will come out more easily;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	and if it is a large bone, like from the leg or thigh, only remove the corruption until all the blackness is gone, then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if a large part of it is corrupted, and it reaches the marrow of the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	it must be scraped and cut all the way to the corruption, and then treated until it is healed;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	and I will tell you about a fistula that occurred in a man's leg, so that you may take example and assistance in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	There was a young man around 30 years old, who had a pain in his leg from a cause that originated within the body, so that the matter went to the leg, and it swelled with a large abscess, and there was no reason to use cautery to open it;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	but the physicians, through their foolishness, worked on it so much that the abscess opened, and much matter flowed from it, and it became a fistula, and many holes appeared there that all released pus and fluid from the body;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and many physicians applied treatment to it for about two years, and none were skilled in the art of surgery, until I was called there, and saw his leg and the medicines with which it was being treated, and what flowed from the holes in large quantity;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the young man's body became red, and he had a jaundiced complexion.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I inserted a tent into one of these holes, and then probed all the holes, and found that they all connected to each other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	I hastened then, and cut into one of the holes until I uncovered a part of the bone, and found it corrupted and perforated, and the corruption went down to the bone inside;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I scraped away what appeared to me of the corrupted bone, and thought there was no other corruption besides what I removed;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I began to treat the wound with cleansing medicines for a long time, and it would not heal;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and then I began again, and uncovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continuing in the bone, and I scraped it, and then removed it, and I tried to heal the place;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	but I could not until I cut around a handspan of bone, and pulled it out completely bare, then treated it with medicines;
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and it was quickly healed and closed, and there was no need to begin the work again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure it, and for the fear of death I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For because of the bloodletting he often sobbed, but he was completely healed, and in place of the bone grew hard flesh, and it was of good quality and he had no harm or discomfort whatsoever, neither in going nor in coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated in this manner:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	Take a linen cloth and tie it to the end of the exposed bone, and instruct someone to pull it upwards;
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and put another woolen tie, thicker than the first, and tie it over the flesh that is above the bone, and pull on the end, so that you draw the damaged flesh underneath, and uncover the flesh on the area where you want to treat, so that the silk does not injure the flesh; 
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and put a firebrand or a board under the bone so that you can easily cut the damaged flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it should be treated as long as one can see and feel the infection, and treated again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	And if the bone is infected, and it is not visible, and the infection is in the middle or in one part, then uncover all the flesh;
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	then place a firebrand underneath, and then treat with silk from one side of the infection to the other, and the silk should be a bit longer than the infection, as we have said; 
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the infection is in the joint, then cut the infected joint, and treat the bone where it connects to the other part; 
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the infection is in the connection of the two joints, then there is no other solution than to cut;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	and if the infection is in the wrist of the hand, or in the ankle of the foot, then this is very difficult, but nevertheless you must investigate this corrosion, as it appears to you; 
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and clean it in all the ways that you can, but so that the veins or the nerves do not cause you difficulty;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and know that the cutting instruments and the saws for cutting these bones are many, depending on the position of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and thinness, and their size, and their hardness; 
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and therefore it is necessary to prepare a suitable instrument for each type of work;
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and know that the work itself will show you the instrument you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the evidence of the types of illnesses;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	so consider the instrument you need according to what is required.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The head can rot either from an internal cause, or from an external cause;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	and when you have treated this decay with medicinal remedies, and they are not effective, then it is necessary to cut off the limb up to the place where the decay reaches, so that the patient escapes death thereby, or by the greater misfortune, the loss of the limb;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	and the sign is that the limb becomes black, so that it seems to be burnt by fire, and rots after the blackness, then this decay spreads from limb to limb, and takes over the whole body;
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	so hasten to cut it off, and if it is from the bite of some venomous beast, like a sea scorpion, viper, or similar, if the decay is at the tip of the finger, cut it off, and do not give it space to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it reaches the hand, cut it off at the joint, so that the decay does not reach the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	and if it reaches the arm, cut it off at the elbow;
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and if it passes the elbow, it is fatal, and no treatment is effective except the extent of its power; (referring to the poison's power)
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	and do the same when the decay occurs in the foot:
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	if it reaches the first joint, cut it off after the next joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it reaches the foot, cut off the whole foot;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it rises into the leg, amputate at the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it goes above the knee, there is no other option but to leave the patient to die;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and the way to cut or saw the limb is that you tie it above and below, and one assistant stretches one of the ties downwards, and another assistant the other tie upwards, and you separate the flesh which is between the two ties with a spatula's width, until the bone is exposed;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	then cut or saw it, and place a linen cloth on each side, so that the saw does not touch the healthy part, and cause the patient further injury and a hot abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	And if bleeding occurs when you operate, cauterize the area quickly, or apply some astringent powders;
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then return to your treatment until it is completed, then tie the wounded limb with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it is healed;
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to a man in his foot:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	he developed a blackness that looked like a burn, and this corrosion started in his toe, until it took over the whole foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the corrosion, he hurried to cut off the foot, and was healed;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and a long time later the corrosion returned in a finger of his hand, and he came to me, and I applied repelling medications after cleansing the body, and the corrosion could not be stopped;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he wanted me to cut off his hand, and I refused, because I had hope of driving back the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	and I also feared that if I cut off his hand, he would die, because the man's constitution was weak;
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he despaired completely, and returned to his land, and hastened to cut off his hand, and was healed;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have only related this so that one may do the same, if there is need.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess arises in a fleshy place, and remains so long that it creates a large collection of pus;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then it breaks and bursts, and the pus spurts out, and the place remains empty, like a vessel;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and the skin that is over it is as thin as a delicate cloth, and it does not run down to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such a condition is called a "sinus," and it is not called a "fistula";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so elongated that it reaches down to the bone deeply, it is called a "fistula";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the treatment is that you cut this skin all around, especially when it is thin, like a cloth;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and it will not heal because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if you are confident that the skin will heal, and the corruption is not deep, and the skin is thick with flesh, then treat it with an enema like this:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	observe if the breast is large, and the pus that comes out has a foul odor, then administer an Egyptian medicine enema which is made like this:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	take vinegar, and oil, and litharge, in equal parts, and put them to cook in a vessel over fire, until the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and then take some of this according to your need, and mix it with water and honey, and inject it into the breast with an enema, and constrict the opening;
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and leave the medicine inside for two hours, then extract it by squeezing;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times, until the breast is cleansed, and the pus is removed;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	and sometimes it is cleansed with ash water, when this medicine is not available, and you should take ashes from vine wood, and pour water over them, then strain it, and inject it with an enema, until you know that the breast is well cleansed;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	and if the patient cannot tolerate it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the ash water, then cleanse it with water and honey in which a little litharge has been ground;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	or you cleanse it with mixed honey and wine, because honey has the property of cleansing and washing, and the wine helps dry the breast;
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and when you have done this, and you are confident that the breast is well cleansed, then cleanse it with that which generates flesh in it, and you should take diachylon plaster, and make it with rose oil and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or you cleanse it with some medicines and ointments, whose properties I have described in the treatise on ointments;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	and if the opening of the breast is small, and the tube of the syringe cannot enter, then widen it a little with an iron instrument, and insert a tent of the Egyptian ointment, or basilicon ointment, until it is widened;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the wound is too large, then sew it up and leave only one place where the syringe can enter, and if the opening that drains pus is at the top, make it in the lowest place.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the pus is deep, it does not allow flesh to regenerate;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	and if you cannot cut the breast from below as you wish, then arrange it in such a way that the pus runs to the lowest place, for when the pus is deep, it does not allow flesh to regenerate, and if you cannot cut the breast from below as you wish, arrange it in this way:
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	so that the pus flows easily downwards, and do not leave any of the pus there;
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	and take consolidative medicines to put on the breast, and spread over it a linen cloth that covers the entire breast;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	then cut forcefully around the opening of the breast a little larger than the first, then spread a soothing ointment on another cloth according to the size of the opening, and place it over the opening of the breast to draw out the pus, and do not remove the large cloth except after many days, once;
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and the one that is over the opening of the breast, remove often to remove the pus, and know what flows from the pus, whether it is venom or little or much, or digested, or undigested;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been spread in this way and you see the nature that jumps/pushes on the opening of the breast, then know that the breast is healing, and health is approaching; 
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	and then unbind it in the morning, or the third day, and when you unbind the wound, change to another cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast releases undigested pus after many days, know that the breast will not heal.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if thin venom flows after a long time, do not despair of healing, for health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For there are people whose flesh is slow to regenerate in their wounds, and others who do the opposite; 
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if undigested pus comes out of the breast after many days, know that the breast will not heal;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	and if the breast is slow to heal, and it is prolonged, add medicines that are moist in substance and dry in virtue, like diachylon ointment, for it contains a large amount of vitriol, and that is the last medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take diachylon ointment, and make it with rose oil, and sprinkle it with old wine equal in substance;
puis le confit et en use;	then preserve it and use it;
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	and this same thing does better cooked thickened, when diachylon ointment is not available, or you take myrrh and aloe and incense, and grind it, and powder it over the honey when it is on the fire;
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and then spread it on a cloth, and spread it over the breast, and sometimes administer long birthwort, and roots of celestial lily, which is like vetch flour and centaury;
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	and use it simple or compound:
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	grind them, and make a powder, and put it on the honey I mentioned, and use it;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	and if the treatment is prolonged, and is not cured by this treatment, then know that the corruption is deep, and makes an impression on the bone, or on the hard members, or on the ligaments;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	then treat it for a fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	A panaritium is an abscess that arises under the nail of the thumb, or of the foot, or perhaps arises in other fingers;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and when it is old, and one does not take care of it, a hot abscess arises there, and runs and throws off pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and sometimes runs through it all;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and the corrosion reaches the bone, so that there is a foul-smelling pain, and the end of the finger is swollen, and the color is dark.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have described in the section, and the treatment is not effective, then you must cut away with a knife all the excess that remains of the nail, then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	Cauterization is a great help if the bone is healthy and the nail is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and if the nail presses into the flesh, and begins to prick and wound it, then you must place a thread under the nail that pricks the flesh, and lift it up, and cut that flesh subtly and lightly, and apply burning and corrosive medicines on the remaining flesh to remove it all;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then cut it and extract it out, for as long as the corrupted bone remains, it cannot heal;
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if you see the finger becoming corrupted, then cut it at one of the joints as described previously, then treat it until it is healed;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	And if it is struck and bruised and there is great pain, then you must first bleed it;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	then cut the nail with a sharp spatula, cutting across the top, and be careful that the cut does not reach the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain;
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, then apply something soothing.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of the whitlow of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The extra finger which grows on the hands of some men by chance is entirely fleshy, and sometimes there are some where there are bones, and sometimes there is a nail, and some of them grow at the base of the joint, where the growth is on certain parts of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	The one that grows on some part of the finger does not move, and the one that grows at the joint of the finger, by chance moves;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The removal of the one that is fleshy is easy, in this way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Cut it at its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	The one that grows at the base of the joint is difficult to treat:
si te tien dou coper.	so refrain from cutting it.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the one that grows in the finger at the last joint, you must first cut the flesh roundly down to the bone, then cut the bone with a saw suitable for this, then treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The fusion that occurs in the fingers together comes by birth, or by the healing of a wound, or by a burn from fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	You must cut this fusion, so that the fingers return to their natural shapes;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then put between the two spaces tents or cloths soaked in rose oil, so they don't fuse back together;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you put between the two thin pieces of lead, until the place is healed, as is necessary.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If fusion occurs in any of his fingers with the palm, cut this fusion as needed.
des vils	of the eyes
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Worms are large convoluted veins full of melancholic superfluities, which appear in several parts of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and occurs more in the legs of those who walk and who work and carry things, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you sometimes administer a purgative of bile, and then heal it with basil.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	The iron cure is done in two ways:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	one is that they are cut, and the black blood is drawn out;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other way is that you lift the vein, and pull it all the way out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The cut is made in this way:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	first bathe the leg with very hot water, until the thick blood is thinned, then tighten the patient's leg from above the thigh down to the part below the knee;
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then cut the vein in one place, or in two or in three, with a wide cut, then lift and draw out the black blood with your hand, from one end to the other, until as much blood comes out as the patient's strength can bear;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then tie it off, and instruct him to abstain from foods that generate black bile;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and repeat the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, and it harms the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The raising of it is in this manner:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	Raise the patient's leg, if there is a lot of hair, then put it in the bath, and sprinkle the leg with hot water until it becomes red, and the veins swell;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you don't have a bath, warm it by the fire, and then cut it along the vein from the thigh to the top of the knee, or in the lower part at the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then open the skin with the hook, and scrape the vein on each side, until it appears when you feel it;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and it appears red and black, and when it enters the skin it looks like a white cord; 
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	then push the thread underneath, until it is lifted from the skin, and then hang it on the hook gently, then cut it in another place about three fingers above;
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then scrape the skin above the vein until it appears, then lift it with the thread, as you did before, and hang it on another hook, as you did the first time;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	then make another cut, or several if you need them, then lift it and cut it with your toe, then pull and lift it up to the second cut;
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then pull it from cut to cut, until it comes out completely, then cut it;
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and if you cannot pull and lift it, then insert a needle with a strong double thread, and tie it and pull it, and put a thread underneath, and turn your hand from side to side, until it comes out;
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and be careful not to cut it, because if it is cut, it cannot be pulled or lifted, and it will harm the patient;
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	and when you have pulled it all out, then put on the wound site wool soaked in wine and rose oil;
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if the penis is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must split it carefully, but do not cut it;
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	and pull it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron with which the penis is cut is curved, and does not cut, so that it does not cut the vein; 
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and it has a large curve, for if it were thin, it would cut the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and here is the shape:
de la voinne civile	of the vein of the penis
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein appears on legs, in hot areas where neither grass nor trees grow, and in land without moisture;
