et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	and sometimes it appears elsewhere than on the legs, and this happens from the putrefaction that comes under the skin, as it occurs inside the body with snakes and worms, generated between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And the sign of the beginning of this vein is that a very large inflammation appears on the leg, then the location changes, and the vein begins to protrude, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the head appears, you must wrap around it a piece of lead weighing from one and a half to two drams, and tie it, and let the lead hang from the leg, and each time it protrudes more when cauterizing, wrap it around the lead, and tie it;
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, cut off a part, and wrap the remainder, and do not cut it at its root, until it is completely removed; 
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cut it, it will go back into the flesh, and cause an abscess and putrefaction in the area, and a serious illness;
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	therefore it must be pulled little by little until the end, and nothing remains in the body;
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	and this vein is sometimes when pulled five palms long, or ten, and a man once came to me, from whom it emerged ten palms long, and when you cut it, insert a probe into the hole, and pierce it all the way through, so that it all comes out;
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	and the matter within should be emptied, and apply medicines generating pus to the area for a few days, then treat it like abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And sometimes this vein has several branches, and especially when it appears in the joint of the foot, or in the foot, and many holes appear there, from which branches emerge;
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	then treat it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This disease is called in our land "ox disease," because it often happens to oxen, and it is a small worm that arises between skin and flesh, and travels throughout the whole body ascending and descending, and one feels it well as it moves from limb to limb, until it breaks the skin where it goes, and jumps out;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and it is generated from the corruption of certain humors, as worms and snakes and earthworms and ascarides arise in the belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	and one fears its malice, for when it travels through the body, and it rises to the head, and it comes to the eye, perhaps it enters and destroys the eye;
et ceu avient maintes fois.	and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you wish to treat it and extract it, you can only do so when it moves:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	therefore, you must tie the area above and below with a strong ligature very tightly, then cut into it and pull it out, and if the worm is deep in the flesh, and you cannot find it, cauterize it with fire on top, until it dies;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that it does is that it infects the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming to the head near the eye, squeeze the eyebrow tightly below it, then cut into it and pull it out;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and the patient must use body cleansing with laxative medicines for the bad putrid humors, and abstain from foods generating rot.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from flatulence
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This illness is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that arises in certain limbs, and then moves from limb to limb;
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and I saw what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm;
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	and shortly after, I saw it rise like a worm to the shoulder, faster than anything, like quicksilver when it runs from place to place;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	the pain left that place, and settled in the shoulder, and then a little later ran throughout the body, until it came to the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me that it constantly moved around the body, as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly how it moved thus from limb to limb, for I had never seen this illness in this way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	However, I had often seen that pain could move from place to place, but I had not seen it as I saw it in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and I thought that this was because the woman had a dry body, and uncovered veins, and because of this, this constrained flatulence appeared;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and it does not appear in this way in those who are soft/delicate, and who have moist bodies and hidden veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you want to treat this illness, and the patient feels this pain, if it appears to you as we have said, then quickly tie it above and below, and then cut into it so that this constrained flatulence at that place can come out;
et cauterize le leu;	and cauterize the place;
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	and if you do not see it with your own eyes, treat it with something that expels flatulence, like fetid pills, and pills of serapin, and other similar things.
des saiettes	of arrows/arrowheads
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows/arrowheads are diverse, according to their appearance and according to the places of the body where they fall.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	Their diversity is such that there are some that have large points, and small, and barbed, and solid/unbarbed;
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and some that have two barbs, and some that have tongues/blades, and some that are in pieces;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	and one that falls into any limb falls in two ways:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	either it falls into a principal member, such as the brain, heart, liver, lung, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members/organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls then into any of these places/organs, and the signs of death, which I will tell you hereafter, appear:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	then you must refrain from extracting this arrow, for death follows in many forms/cases;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when these bad signs do not appear, and the arrow is not embedded deeply, then draw it out, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the sign of the brain when the arrow falls there and pierces the bone, and the dura mater, which is over the brain, bursts out, is when there is dizziness and stupor and vertigo and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile; 
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	and perhaps blood comes out of the nostrils, or the ears;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps he loses speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and from the wound comes a white moisture resembling pus, and also something like burnt flesh comes out;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if these signs appear to you, abstain from treatment, and pull out the arrow if it is not inside.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs of an arrow when it falls into the heart, are that it is near the left nipple, and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not hollow; 
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and sometimes the arrow moves like the pulse, and black blood flows, and coldness comes with a cold sweat, and fainting:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	know then without a doubt that death is coming.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow that injures the lung is that blood mixed with froth comes from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and sighs deeply and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the arrow falls into the covering of the chest, it is near the small ribs;
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	and causes great difficulty breathing, great pain and sighing;
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	and all the limbs from the shoulders down twitch/tremble.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow falls into the stomach, perhaps some undigested food will come out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow falls into the belly, and some excrement comes out of the wound through a ruptured intestine, there is no hope in the treatment, nor in extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and urine comes out of the wound, and the patient feels severe pain:
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the face, neck, throat, shoulders, armpits, spine, ribs, thighs, legs, and similar parts, are safe according to various factors.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a man that an arrow struck him in the tear duct at the root of the nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I probed it, and drew it out on the other side under the fat of the ear, and he was healed without harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And I pulled out, as a game, an arrow that had fallen into the fat of the eye, below the lower eyelid, and the arrow was lodged, and I could only reach the tip towards the shaft, and the arrow was a large one from a Turkish bow, with a light, smooth iron head without barbs;
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	the eye was healed, and no ill effects occurred.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And I pulled an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arabian arrow with barbs:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I filed down the barbs, and worked carefully until I pulled it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I removed an arrow from a man, that had fallen into his belly, and I thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and after thirty days had passed, his condition did not change;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut down upon the arrow, and manipulated it, and pulled it out, and there were no ill effects.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And I also saw a man who had an arrow fall into his back, and the wound closed over it;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and the arrow remained inside him, and he did not change his natural habits, nor did he find harm in any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And I saw another man, who had an arrow fall into his face, and the wound closed;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and it remained thus without causing him great pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	and many other similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And I extracted an arrow from one of the king's princes, which had fallen into the middle of his nose, and was slightly inclined to the right side;
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and the arrow was completely embedded.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called to treat it three days after it had fallen.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I searched for it with a very fine probe, and did not feel it;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt a prick and pain under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was from the arrowhead. I applied an attractive and digestive plaster to the area, so that the place would not swell;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and the location of the arrow appeared to me.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I put the plaster there for several days, and the wound healed over again, and the patient remained like this for a long time, until he felt the arrow one day inside his nose; 
et il le me dist.	and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I applied a sharp corrosive medicine to the wound for several days, until it was open, and I probed it, and felt the head of the arrow, which was stuck in place;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I added more of that sharp medicine into the opening of the wound, until the head of the arrow became clearly visible to me;
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and the time period certainly exceeded four months, and then the wound widened enough so that I inserted the forceps, and moved it back and forth, but it could not come out;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	then I did not cease to refine and devise different kinds of instruments, until one day I grasped it with well-made forceps, according to the form that will appear at the end of this chapter, until I pulled it out, and healed the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And physicians believe that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	then I restored it, and the wound was sutured, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	Now I have told you about the nature of extracting some arrows, so you should apply your care to that which I have not mentioned, because the book cannot include everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	but the wise master understands much from little, and based on what is present and lacking, finds new work, and new instruments, for the removal of strange things that occur in this art. 
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows do not emerge from the limbs where they are embedded except in two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	either through the place where they entered, or through another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and the one that comes out through where it entered is an arrow entering fleshy places, and sometimes comes out immediately.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not come out immediately, leave it until the flesh around it rots, and the exit is widened; 
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if it is embedded in the bone, and it cannot come out, leave it like that for some days, and move it every day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it will come out, and if it does not, then pierce around it entirely with a thin drill, until the place around it is widened, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow is embedded in the bone of the head, and goes down to one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the symptoms that I have mentioned appear in the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	do not pull it out, but leave it until it becomes even after some days, because if the arrow reaches the dura mater, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is only embedded in the bone, and does not reach the dura mater, and the patient remains for some days without ill effects, then devise a way to pull it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is embedded very deeply like that and cannot come out easily, then apply drills around it, as I have told you;
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the area until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is lodged in a place on the body where it cannot be seen, then search for it with the probe;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, then pull it out with a suitable instrument; 
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound, and because of the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone or nerve or vein there, then enlarge the wound until it is large enough;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and pull the arrow out if you can, and if the arrow has barbs which are holding it in, then remove the flesh which is pierced on both sides as best you can, and then break or bend the barbs of the arrow, so that you can pull it out;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and take care not to break the arrow, as you would have more difficulty removing it.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, leave it until the place around it is putrid, then pull it out, because the extraction will be easier. 
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the flow of blood opposes you, then administer what we have said about the treatment in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	and beware of cutting a nerve or a vein, and strive how you can best remove the arrow without danger, either quickly or slowly, firmly or gently;
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	and position the patient in the same way he was when the arrow struck him, for this is the greatest help there is, and if you cannot, then place him according to what the signs indicate.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	An arrow that comes out from another part, where any part of it is visible, or the skin is swollen around it so that it can be clearly seen or felt: 
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	then cut into it, until the forceps can grasp it, and then extract it:
si saut fuer maintenant.	if it jumps out immediately.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, then rotate your hand circularly, until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, leave it again, and then recommence the extraction until it comes out;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the shaft of the arrow is there, push it out with the entire shaft;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	and if the shaft falls, and you want to administer pushing, then apply a threaded instrument, so that the point of the arrow enters the threading of the instrument;
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and then push it out, and if the arrow is barbed, push in a pointed instrument, to facilitate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is poisoned, you must cut away all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow falls into the chest, or the belly, or the bladder, or the side, and it is close, and you can cut down to it, then cut;
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and be careful not to cut the vein or the nerve, and then extract it, and then sew the wound, if necessary;
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps with which one draws out arrows are similar to a bird's beak, and here is the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And there are many kinds:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the pushing instrument is like the feather of a bird, to push against the tip of the arrow, as is the shape here:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the forceps for pushing and for pulling is here:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	There are 31 veins from which one bleeds, of which 16 are in the head, namely:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	Two pulsating veins which are behind the ears, which are called the two "arteries behind the ear";
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and the two arteries which are visible in the two temples;
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins which are in the two tear ducts of the two eyes, which are called "corner veins";
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein which is at the tip of the nose;
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two jugular veins that are in the neck;
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are in the upper lips of the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich"; (possibly referring to the superior labial veins)
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The veins from which one commonly bleeds are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic, and it is on the left side, and the lay people call it the "head vein";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	and the middle one is called "faste," and it is composed of the cephalic and the basilic, and the lay people call it the "heart vein";
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and the basilic is on the right side, and the lay people call it the "belly vein", and it is above the elbow, and it is the one from which one bleeds, which appears clearly on the wrist.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the salvatella is the vein which is between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	and in the leg and foot there are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	one is below the curve of the wrist on the left side, and the second, the saphenous, which is at the ankle on the right side;
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the vein which is called "nesse," which is on the ankle of the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg there are three veins below these.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	Bleeding the veins that are behind the ears helps with chronic catarrh and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	and the way to bleed them, as I tell you, is that you raise the patient's head and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth;
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	then have the patient tighten their neck by screwing their head, until the two veins appear behind the ears in two places hanging from the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	then search for them with your finger, and where you feel the pulse under your finger, bleed with a lancet;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	then take the lancet, and push it under the vein down to the bone, then lift your hand with the vein upwards, and cut both the skin and the vein well the width of two fingers, and let out as much blood as you see fit;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then bandage and tie it until it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already discussed incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	Bleeding the two arteries that are in the two temples is beneficial for chronic and sudden migraines, and habitual ophthalmia, and for a burning sensation of sharp tears in the eyes;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the method of bleeding is as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is that the patient strains his neck until the two veins appear clearly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feel the pulse under your finger, and then bleed with a lancet;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	then lift the skin above the vein upwards with your index finger, and insert the lancet underneath, and lift the vein upwards, and cut it, as you have done with the two other veins, and let the blood flow according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then untie the patient, and put your finger over the vein for an hour, then apply cotton;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	and then bind it tightly, and leave it until it is healed;
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and we have already spoken of them and of their cutting and their extraction, at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	Bleeding from the vein of the forehead is as effective as bleeding from the cephalic vein for long-standing illnesses of the face, and for migraines, and for redness;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the procedure is that the patient strains his neck by twisting, until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument which is called "digger," of which here is the form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point on the vein, and strike upon it with your hand, or with something else, and let the blood flow out according to the quantity you desire;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then release the patient's neck, and tie off the vein until it is healed, and sometimes it is opened with a broad lancet.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	However, it is not necessary that the lancet be too sharp;
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	and cut across it, because the bone is near, and perhaps the lancet breaks when it is thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	Bleeding the two veins that are in the two tear ducts helps the eyes, and against ringworm, and redness, and sty in the eye, and diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the manner of bleeding them is that the patient strains his neck by twisting with some bandage, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then bleed him, and let the incision be across, a little along the lancet a little wide, for there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the lancet is thin, perhaps it will break;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	then let the blood flow as much as you need, and then apply cotton on it, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	Bleeding from the vein of the nose is good for acute illness, and sudden madness, and diseases of the face, such as migraine and redness that comes to the face, and especially when it is chronic;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	and the way to perform the bleeding is that the patient tightens his neck, then you hold his nose with your left hand, and take the thin long lancet, and insert it in the middle of the lip in the space that is between the two nostrils, because the vein does not appear well there, and the blood will immediately begin to flow;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not go too deep, and let the blood flow according to your need, then tie it up for a night, because it is very quickly restored;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the shape of the lancet:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	Bleeding from the two tonsils helps with shortness of breath, and the onset of leprosy, and many illnesses, and impetigo, and corrosive ulcers, and herpes, and malignant ulcers;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the way to perform the bleeding is that the patient stretches his neck below both, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	and let the practitioner stand above the patient's head, and let the patient sit on a seat, then bleed the vein lengthwise a little widely, then draw blood moderately, or as much as is needed;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	then do the same in the other vein, then untie the ligature, and compress both veins moderately, so that the patient does not choke;
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and leave it until morning, so that the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the bleeding of the lips
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	Bleeding the upper lip veins helps with glue in the mouth, and with corruption of the gums, and cracked lips, and the nose and around it.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the way to perform the bleeding is to have the patient sit in front of you, and compress his neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one of which is on the right lip and the other on the left, and they are recognizable because they are black, and because around them are small black veins:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	then cut one and the other, and if you do not recognize them, and you are in doubt, cut the largest one on each side, and do the same for the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the bleeding under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	Bleeding the veins that are under the tongue helps after bleeding the cephalic vein, and this is for tightening of the throat, and for diseases of the uvula, and for diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the proper way to bleed is that the patient sits between your hands in front of the sun, and lifts their tongue, and you look underneath on each side for a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	bleed then one and the other, and do not go too deep, because underneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins of the neck that are commonly bled are bled in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	either by pricking with a myrtle-leaf-shaped lancet, broad, or a subtle olive-shaped one like cutting edges, and it is called "anesil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are broad and narrow according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The myrtle leaf shape is very renowned, and is broad as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is needed for opening hairy veins full of visible thick blood, and that contain thick and turbid blood;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the shape of the olive-shaped lancet:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more finely pointed, and it is for bleeding thin veins, where there is thin, clear blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	Bleeding from the basilic vein, which is one of these veins, helps with illnesses that are below the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the belly;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and the bloodletter must bleed wisely, and beware of the artery that is beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and bleeding occurs, then it must be stopped, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and the blade should not be piercing, but cutting like a lancet.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilic vein is not clearly visible, then you must compress it, and choose another;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	or you look for a branch of it, or you bleed from the vein in the middle of the arm instead:
elle apert manifestement;	it is clearly visible;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and make the incision with the lancet blade, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you wish to know the place for the bloodletting, you must first, before tightening the arm, touch the area until you feel the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the place with ink, and then tie the arm, and cut the vein with the lancet blade;
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	and be careful not to strike the artery when you see the place swollen, for that is the artery:
eschui la donques.	then wipe it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it spurt upwards like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is blood from the artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	hurry then, and put your finger on it for a long time, then remove your finger if the blood stops, which often happens; 
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	then bind the arm, and leave it like that, and let the patient not move it;
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let him be careful, and not move it until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	And if the blood is not stopped, and it overcomes you, and the medicine is not at hand, then cut the artery if it is visible, for the ends will retract; 
et estainche li sans.	and the blood will stop.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a rind of green stick, and split it, and take one of the halves and tie it on firmly until the next day;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	if the blood stops, that is good;
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if not, then treat it, as we have said, with powders that stop blood;
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and stopping the bleeding is not difficult in most cases because of the small size of the wound, and the strength of the arm's ligature.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The median vein bleeding in the middle is helpful as it draws blood from the head above and from the body below, because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and the bloodletter must be cautious of the nerve that is underneath, and if he punctures too deep, and he finds the nerve, and it swells and healing is difficult, and perhaps it cannot heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	and this nerve is apparent many times, and if it is not apparent in some men due to its thinness, then you must bleed it with a lancet instrument; 
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and avoid the nerve as much as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between two nerves, then open it lengthwise.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	Bleeding from the cephalic vein is helpful, as it draws blood from the head, and helps the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and one should bleed by puncturing at the site of the olive leaf or the myrtle leaf, because it is the safest of all the veins, for there is neither nerve nor artery beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, one should seek the easiest location, and it doesn't matter if one misses the first time, and starts again;
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and perhaps the area swells in some people, when one misses the first time, but it doesn't matter.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The amount of bloodletting depends on your judgment.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing you must know about bloodletting is that it is administered only to maintain health, and to avoid future illnesses;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	and the bloodletting should be done in one of the three veins that are in the elbow:
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	that is to say, cephalic, median cubital, and basilic;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one should be bled at the beginning of spring on an empty stomach, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of plethora appear;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	and one should be bled on the first or third day, after two or three hours of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	Bloodletting that is administered for illnesses has no fixed time, but rather when there is need, day or night, at all hours and at all times;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and one should not bleed children until fourteen years old, nor pregnant women except from the fourth month until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Nor should the elderly who are past sixty years old be bled.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when someone wants to be bled, in whatever manner it may be, they should cleanse the intestines with a light enema, if they have much retained stool, so that the veins do not draw from the intestines putrid superfluities harmful to the principal members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	nor should one bleed someone who is overly satiated with food, nor who is drunk, until they are recovered, nor the dropsical;
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and one should beware of bleeding after colic, and vomiting, and diarrhea, and frequent sexual intercourse with a woman, and from exertion, from staying awake, and from fasting, and that which weakens all strength, whether by something of the mind or of the body;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then thin the humors, if the blood is thick, through foods and drinks and through medicines, if you have the means;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	then enter the bath, if nothing prevents it, to thin the blood, and be bled from the vein of the chest around the third hour, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and on that day, guard yourself from exertion, and from difficulty, and from sexual activity, and from similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	and be happy and joyful, and let the bloodletter be higher than the one being bled, and let him rub the arm two or three times, then tie the ligature moderately tight, because when it is too tight or too loose, the blood cannot flow;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the area with the hands, until the veins swell, and they can be felt;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	then the bloodletter moistens the lancet with a little old oil, then puts a finger of his left hand on that vein a bit below the place where he wants to bleed, so that the vein does not flee and fail upon being lanced.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	For there are veins that flee like cords when being bled, and there are some that are full of wind, so that when one places the lancet upon them, it withdraws the lancet and the vein cannot be opened, and thus it is with these; 
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if he opens the vein, the wound is too narrow, therefore the bloodletter must be knowledgeable in these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if the vein opens the first time, that is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	if not, then start again a little below that place or quickly above, if the place is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the place is swollen, and the patient is frightened, let him be for a day or two, and do not bind the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	perhaps hot abscesses will develop there;
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	do not enter the bath, then resume the bleeding if it pleases him;
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the opening is small, or the blood flows thinly and you doubt that not enough blood will come out as you wish, then strike in that same opening with the entire blade directly;
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	and work a little hastily, before the place swells;
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	for this often happens, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the place swollen, do not restart the bleeding, and put on a little oil lees, for it lightens the body of blood, and the lees are better in this place than the oil;
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer the oil lees in every bleeding that you bleed from the veins, to staunch the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	and theriac does the same, and ox dung, when it is put on the place;
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	thus the blood thins and spreads when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if there comes a large abscess, which happens often, especially when it is not bled except at the time when the opening of the vein is small, then hurry, and put on the place a sponge moistened in slightly warm water and salt, and squeeze it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and you must do this after the blood has flowed from the vein, and if any blackness or greenness remains at the place after a few days, it does not harm it;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you wish, put on something of aloes or myrrh mixed in juice of calamint, mountain mint, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And often an abscess and swelling appear at the opening of the basilic vein:
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	then put your hand on it, and if you find the place soft under the pressure of the hand, this swelling is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	Be careful then that you do not apply any of the things that we have mentioned, for perhaps it cuts into the artery;
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	but make a dry plaster to harden the place, then treat it with other remedies, until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw blood from each finger according to the strength of its vein, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it is red;
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	and if you see it thick, let it flow until it is thinned;
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And for one who is full and strong, and needs bloodletting, a larger wound should be made, and the lancet should be wide;
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and he should be bled little and often, and he should be bled by cutting across, not by pricking;
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this method of bleeding is safe from excessive bleeding and severing a nerve, and is better than bleeding along the length or width.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	And to one whose body fails during bleeding, give bread soaked in pomegranate juice;
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	if he is feverish, then draw blood three or four times. And if he is of a cold complexion, have him eat before bleeding bread soaked in muscat syrup, or in honey syrup flavored with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and a fragrant syrup. 
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints during bleeding, after the loss of much blood, he should drink meat broth, and a fine, fragrant syrup, and use the other things that we have mentioned in the section or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of a vein. 
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to air out his arm and bleed again, he should, when he is weakened by extensive bleeding, bleed little by little, according to the extent of his strength, continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wishes to air out their arm after the first bleeding, and has a strong constitution, let them bleed seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to be bled from another location, should be bled on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	For there is much blood within the body that is already heated, and causes fever;
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	so a large quantity must be drawn, and the opening widened until he falls into a faint;
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	then, as you observe all the conditions of bleeding, and place your hand on his pulse as he bleeds, so that death does not come instead of fainting, and this happens many times, when the bloodletter is negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it is not appropriate, when you wish to untie the arm, and let the blood flow a second time, and the opening is closed, that you press firmly on it;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	nor if it is bent, that he extend the arm hastily, for that would be bad;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	but leave it until it bleeds a second time;
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	or you prick it with the point of the lancet, until the blood that is congealed at the opening of the vein comes out, and put on it a little salt dissolved in water, and press lightly on it.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it and do not constrict it, until the swelling has subsided.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, bleed it in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the middle of the arm is bled instead of the vein of the head because it is well-suited.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of the bloodletting is that the patient puts his hand in warm water, until the vessels are red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then it should be moderately tied, so that the vein appears well, then bleed it immediately across, not lengthwise nor widely;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and let the opening be wide, and be bled very near the joint of the hand, and if blood cannot come out, put the hand back in warm water, and let the blood run into the water, until you have enough;
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is in summer, do not put the hand back in warm water, for it is put there more in winter than in summer;
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and bleeding from this vein is safer than all other veins, because there is neither artery nor nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	Bleeding from the cephalic vein of the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is the method:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	bind the hand, and put it in warm water, until the vein is swollen, so that it can be seen;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and bleed it across, and if you cut it completely through, it does no harm;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and do not go too deep, for the nerves are underneath, bare of flesh, and then put the hand back in warm water, if the blood is congealed in the wound, and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn as much blood as is necessary, put oil and salt on the vein to heal it quickly, and do so for each branch.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	Bleeding it in the left hand is good for diseases of the spleen, and do just as I told you on the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	Bleeding the saphenous vein is good for all illnesses that are below the body, such as illnesses of the marrow, and retention of menses, and illnesses of the kidneys, and of the thighs and of old legs, and similar illnesses.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the way to bleed it is that the patient puts his foot in warm water, and rubs the vein until it appears, and ties above the ankle joint;
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and the vein is at the ankle, and many branches go above the foot;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	bleed it then in the largest branch, or at the ankle, which is better.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you bleed it above the foot, beware of the nerves that are below, and bleed it across as if cutting; 
et soit li flaimes anesil.	and let the lancet be sharp.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, put the foot back in the water, and let the vein empty well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the bloodletter misses the first time, repeat the second time a little above, because the area is safe;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	do not fear the nerve, as we have said, and do the same with the saphenous vein of the other foot likewise. 
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The location of the sciatic vein is at the ankle outside, and its bleeding is beneficial for hip pain, when it is due to hot blood. 
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the way to bleed it is that the patient enters the bath, and squeezes above the ankle four fingers' width by twisting, for otherwise the vein does not appear;
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	and if it appears, bleed it in every way you can, and across;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it is better that you cut it, for the location is safe, and it is greatly renowned among many men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find it, bleed any branch of it that appears on the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	and let as much blood flow as you wish, and then untie the ligature, and apply cotton and tighten it;
ele est maintenant sanee.	it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of cupping bleeds
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Cupping glasses are made of horn, or brass, or glass;
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	and cupping is done in two ways:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	either by lancing and drawing blood, or without lancing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this cupping without lancing is done in two ways:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	either with fire, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	and cupping done by lancing and drawing blood is done in fourteen places on the body, one of which is right on the top of the head;
et li autres est emmi le col;	and the other is in the middle of the neck;
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and two others on the two sides of the neck;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the cupping glass under the chin;
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the cupping glasses on the two shoulders;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the cupping glasses on the buttocks;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and the cupping glasses in the middle of the two arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and the cupping glasses on the two legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and the cupping glasses on the two ankles;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and cupping does not draw blood, except from the small veins that are spread in the flesh, and therefore one does not weaken from it, as one does from bloodletting from a vein;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it should not be administered, neither with fire nor without fire, in any illness that comes from plethora, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of illness cupping is required, or by habit, we administer it every time at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in the middle, and at any time;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are some who, when they need cupping, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and there are some who find fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and in the neck, and darkness in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and some who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have a swollen tongue, and cough up blood; 
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are some who dream, and see at night blood and wounds and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is in the middle of the month, we order them to be cupped after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The bloodletting of the nose helps with the heaviness of the head ... that comes to the eyes, and it is not necessary that this be after the evacuation of the whole body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and this cupping is in place of the bleeding of the cephalic vein, and it is not appropriate for those of a cold complexion to use it, or those who have catarrh, because it causes them great harm; 
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and therefore it is not appropriate for the elderly to use it, nor those who have cold illnesses in the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And he who is often bled becomes forgetful, and therefore it is necessary to place the cupping glass a little lower for fear of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	Cupping in the middle of the neck is in place of bleeding from the head and the basilic vein, and therefore it is good for tightness of the chest, and for cracking of the bronchial tube, and for coughs, and for congestion;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and there one should apply it lightly, because if it holds too firmly, it generates forgetfulness in the stomach and in the heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	Cupping on the two sides of the neck is good for headaches, and ophthalmia and migraine, and for sore throat, and for pain in the roots of the teeth, and is in place of bleeding from the basilic vein;
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and you must instruct the bleeder to loosen his hand when applying it, so that he does not cut the artery, and there is no excessive bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	Cupping under the chin is good for diseases of the mouth, and for corruption of the gums, and similar illnesses that are in the mouth;
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	and is in place of bleeding from the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Cupping on the shoulders is good for illness that comes from heat and plethora.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	Cupping on the elbows is worth as much as from the three veins of the arm, because it draws blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instruct the bleeder not to strike too deeply, for the place is bare of flesh, and has nerves and arteries underneath.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The cupping glass that is placed on the buttocks is good for hemorrhoids of the anus, and for illnesses below, and it is necessary that the cupping glass be large, and made of brass, because it needs to draw well; 
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	and perhaps, if it were thin, it would break;
et i fai grans plaies.	and make large wounds there.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	Cupping glasses on the legs bleed openly, for they draw blood from the whole body, and are good for old pains of the loins, and of the spleen, and of the bladder, and restore menstruation;
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	and are placed at the location of the two saphenous veins, and the two ankles, and nevertheless they weaken the body after long use, and cause fainting in many ways.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The way to apply the cupping glass is that you first place it empty, and suck moderately, and place it quickly, and move it evenly, and do not stop doing this until you see the place red and swollen, and the redness of the blood appears;
