puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	then cauterize, and replace the cupping glasses, and take care in the disposition of the bodies, because there are some who have tender flesh and clear pores:
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	so it is necessary to strike only once, and make wide wounds, and a little deep;
et suce legierement.	and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to strike twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	the first time to thin the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to strike a third time;
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	and when we want to draw blood little by little, striking once is sufficient. 
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we want a lot of blood, we start again often;
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and if the blood is thick, strike deeply, and the limit is that the heart be pierced suddenly, and for those who have thick and hard skin, and who have narrow pores, you should anoint the places of the cupping glasses with opening and dissolving oil:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in summer, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or oil of cucurbita seed;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in winter, with watercress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluity is thick and cold, take marjoram oil, or balsamite oil, or dill oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one being treated has tender flesh and large pores, no oil should be applied, but it should be washed after cupping with rose water, or cold water, or nightshade water, or cucurbita water, or purslane water, or similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture, should rinse with vinegar, or myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have thick superfluities should rinse with old wine, or elderflower water, or a decoction of dill or chamomile, or other similar things;
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	and one should not be treated with cupping before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath an hour or two;
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and should not sleep after cupping, and must take care when he is to be cupped and when he has been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And be wary if the one who is being treated is choleric, and if the blood is too sharp and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	then he should take cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces with vinegar, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and eat chickens, and mutton, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold complexion should take honey syrup, and moderately fragrant wine, which is between old and new, and eat little, and eat chickens and small birds and pigeons;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and the day he is cupped, he should drink more than he eats;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give some men sometimes theriac or nutmeg before cupping, or after, to strengthen the principal members;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and the blood should be thinned, but it is not necessary for those who are hot to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The cups that are applied without scarification are those that are placed over the liver, and over the spleen, and for gout, and over the belly and the buttock and the loins and the hip, because these parts do not tolerate being cut over the skin, and it is only done to draw blood from one part to another, as we place them on the breasts when the nose bleeds;
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	to remove the viscosity that is in the limb, as we put cups on the belly and on the buttock to reduce the limb;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and removes the pain, when there is blockage or stone, thus removes by its attractive power perhaps the blockage, or loosens the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	and so it does when it is placed on the liver and on the spleen when there is retained flatulence, and these cups are applied empty to only suck;
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	and sometimes they are applied together with fire, and sometimes filled with lukewarm water, as in diseases of the pleurisy, and in such a way that one fills the cup with hot water alone, or with water in which suitable herbs have been boiled for this.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The method of the cupping glass applied with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And let it be two fingers wide and half a palm deep, and let it have on the side around the middle a small hole, like for inserting a needle, and let it be made of brass, smooth in front so that it does not injure the patient when placed on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and let it have in the middle a crossbar of brass or iron, to place a lit candle, and let there be both large and small ones according to the illnesses and the age of those who receive them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the cupping glasses for children are different from those for the elderly, and for the thin different from those for the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one should apply this cupping glass to the limb in this way:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	take a wax candle or a wick, and place it in the middle of the cupping glass across the bar which is in the middle of the cupping glass, so that the flame is at the bottom of the cupping glass so that it does not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it on the limb, and your fingers should be over the hole that we mentioned, so that when one wishes, the vapor escapes, and one removes the cupping glass;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and one takes the wick as before, and repeats this often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the cupping glass then which is used in the case of pleurisy, acutely, there is no bar nor hole, and fire is used only when it is full of water, and it is placed only on the limb;
et c’est li forme:	and this is the method:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Leeches are used only on limbs where one cannot place cupping glasses due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar places;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in places devoid of flesh, such as fingers or nose, and other similar places;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the method of use is that when you find leeches that are in clean fresh water without filth, take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them in fresh water for a night, so that they become hungry, and have nothing in their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then be bled by vein or cupping glass, then rub the limb until it is red, and place the leeches on it;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are full, and fall off, if it is a place where one can apply a cupping glass, apply it, for this is very beneficial afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, then wash the area well, first with vinegar, and then with water, and then wipe it; 
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the area bleeds too much after the leeches are removed, wet a linen cloth in cold water, and place it on, until the bleeding has stopped;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the blood flow is excessive, apply crushed vitriol, or gallnuts, and similar things, until it is stopped;
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you can put on the area half of peeled beans, and leave them until they dry on the spot, this will stop it immediately; 
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more, then take other leeches.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the leeches do not want to attach, rub the area with fresh blood, or prick it with a needle until the blood comes out, and then put them on, and as soon as they sense the blood, they will attach;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are falling off, sprinkle on a little aloe and crushed salt, or ash, and they will fall off immediately.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and concerns the repair of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear son, that fools throw themselves into this chapter, who have never seen any of the ancient books, nor read a letter of them;
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason, knowledge is scarce in our land, for I never found any good one;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing of it except through the knowledge of ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have extracted the knowledge, and through experience, and through the practice of my life;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	and I have here described in this chapter what is contained, and have abbreviated it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are administered, as I have done in these two preceding chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we state in the prologue of this book the main points of the discussion and the chapters where the wise man applies his understanding, and dwells on the truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or sprain or break occurs to someone, you must hasten to treat the patient on both sides, unless something prevents you entirely, such as weakness of the body, or infancy, or old age;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	or if the weather is not very hot, or too cold;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and eat cold, thin foods, that is to say, cold broths, and bird and venison meat, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not overfill yourself with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you no longer fear a hot abscess, or the spreading of matter in the limb;
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	then the patient should return to their former diet that they were used to.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that provide substantial nourishment, where there is viscosity, such as wheat cooked in water, and rice, and heads, and feet, and cow's tripe, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with such nourishment, the fracture repairs and heals more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the broken bones of the old and decrepit cannot heal or knit well according to their nature because of the dryness of the limbs, nor can those that are too tender, like the bones of small children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but have no fear, re-align the broken bone, apply a firm splint that supports and binds the limb together, until it strengthens as it was before;
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and do not move it at all from its position, and for this reason it is necessary to nourish it with rich foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For a fracture of the head is different from a fracture of the chest, or of the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes across, and another obliquely, like the cut of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with only a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each type has its own technique and its own specific instrument for restoration, according to what is recalled in its place; 
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and the fracture of the bone is recognized by the fact that the place is twisted, and appears clearly by default, and makes a sound when pressed by the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no twisting or sound on touching, and the patient does not feel much pain, then there is no fracture;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but there may well be twisting, or a fissure, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	So you should not move it with your hand, but apply the medicines that come later, and then immediately bandage it carefully.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that for the fracture that goes across, and the two parts are separated, they must be immediately set evenly, before hot swelling comes there; 
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if hot swelling comes there, leave it for a few days, until the swelling subsides;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	then set it evenly as best you can lightly and carefully, and know that its restoration is easier than the restoration of one where there are pieces; 
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then bandage it, as is appropriate below.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if there are broken pieces in the bone, extend it from two sides, if it is a hand or foot, or with your hand if it is a small limb, or with two cords, or with one cord and your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and place the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken limb are separated, skillfully bring the additional pieces back to their places as best you can, and be careful that your work does not cause the patient injury or pain;
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and carefully join the two ends of the bones in the best possible alignment.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And feel it carefully with your hand if it seems to you that it is not right:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	then straighten it gently, and do not constrict it too much, nor press it as those do who, through their work, cause a hot abscess and contraction in the limb, as we have often seen.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is properly set, warn the patient carefully not to move it, neither while awake nor while sleeping, nor while turning, nor in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and ensure that the limb is so securely positioned that they feel no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when they feel no pain, it is not properly set, and it must be positioned in such a way that they feel no pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and take care that it is set straight, so that no crookedness develops when it is restored;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the characteristics of the broken limb are as I have told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs vary in smallness and largeness and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are small limbs, such as arms and fingers and similar:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	so it is necessary to wrap soft and fine linen cloths;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those that are large, such as the thigh and leg:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	so it is necessary to wrap with a wide and strong bandage, for the wide bandage embraces the whole large limb, and constricts it evenly on all sides, so that there is no unevenness;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then tie around light padding, three or four turns according to the limb, and tighten your hand a little with the whole bandage, then go above the break and tighten less, as the break then moves away from the break a little;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and loosen the bandage little by little, until you take a large part of the healthy area, then take another bandage, and wrap it again over the broken place;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then go back to the part below the break, and tighten it moderately, not too tight nor too loose, as we have said in the first place above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then put between the bandages linen padding or cloths, until it is all even, then tie a bandage over everything, and then put your well-made splints on, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, apply something soothing and warm to the abscess, which removes the swelling, and leave it like that for a few days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then tighten your splints, and they should be wisely cut half the width of a large cane, or from wood which one makes roofing shingles, or from palm branches, and they should be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the splint that is placed over the break be a little thicker and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and be as long as is necessary for the limb, small or large;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then tighten the splints as you did at the first binding, then tie over it a thread suitably, as in the first binding over the fracture;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	narrower above, always less;
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and the threads must be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and be of soft linen;
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the threads are thick, as I have seen in the works of fools who make their bindings with twisted linen cords, and this is a great error, for the binding cannot be even if it is too tight, and there should not be less than a finger's width between each splint.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is injured by the ends of the splints after tightening in healthy places, put linen wads, or carded wool, under them so that he is not hurt.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the fracture, and the heart is broken, I will discuss the treatment hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not appropriate to bind all fractured limbs with splints on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limb is large, splints should not be applied until after five or seven days, or more depending on your certainty of a hot abscess arising;
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	and see here the method of ancient plasters to restore fractures, dislocations, and sprains:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and you should take the flour that sticks to the walls of the mill, and mix it with plenty of eggs, and apply this mixture, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common way of the plaster restoring the fracture in many cases, and especially in women and small children, because it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another method of plaster restoring fracture and dislocation and sprain:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	take three of abaris and labdanum and elecampane and asafetida and gum arabic and musk, each ten drams;
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	myrrh and aloes, each five drams;
alechil VIIII З.;	mastic nine drams;
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	and make them into a powder, and mix them with egg white;
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	if the person's complexion is hot, then use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and quickly restores broken bones, and is beneficial for many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another type of plaster that is good for sprains:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	take mugwort and marshmallow, each ten drams;
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	myrrh and aloe, each nine drams;
acaice VI З.;	acacia, six drams;
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Armenian bole, ten drams, and grind well, and mix with water or egg white, and apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another kind of plaster for joints and bones separated from their places, and soothes the resulting pain, and the cut from the bone, and the break:
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	take new wool, and soak it in vinegar and cooked oil, and put it on the place.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not restore, but it is good for soothing a hot abscess, and cleanly removes the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another kind of plaster that restores broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	take dried fig leaves, and ground ivy leaves, and grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another kind of plaster for the restoration of a bone fracture and to diminish the remains of the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take marshmallow root, chamomile, violet flowers, vetch flour, one part of each;
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	and grind, and mix with wine, and if the limb is inflamed, mix it with coriander water, or with water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another kind of plaster, stronger than the first, when a hard abscess comes at the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take marshmallow roots, and flax seed, pomegranate rind, melilot, and elderflower, and violet and chamomile flowers, equal parts of all;
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	and grind, and mix with salt water, or fresh water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates said in his book that one should not put on a broken limb to restore it anything but a cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else more, and said that it should be between the two, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And Galen seems to say that one should put on a broken limb, to restore it, somewhat warm dry things, such as myrrh and aloe and frankincense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another type of plaster that is good for injury and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	take mugwort and cut human hair, or bird feathers, and marshmallow, and salt equally, and grind them, and make a plaster and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then unbind it a little later, and take care if the patient feels any pain, or if the bone has moved from its place;
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	if not, do not untie it for many days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain comes to the place, or itching, without rest or swelling, then hurry, and untie it, and remove the plaster immediately;
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	and take a light cloth, and a moist sea sponge, and dip it in water, and wash the area, until the itching stops, and the pain is soothed;
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then let the limb rest for an hour, then apply dry wool, moistened in water or rose oil, and bind it overnight, until you are sure of a warm abscess;
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	and the inflammation of the limb subsides, and the pain is removed, then begin again the fine binding, and a little of the plaster, and do not tighten it as much as before;
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and continue gradually until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the warm abscess and redness and pain and swelling are completely gone, and you need plaster and bandage, then start again, just as you did the first time.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if the limb does not experience any of what we have described, do not unbind it until after three or four or five or seven days;
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	and sometimes leave it for twenty days, depending on what one sees, until the fracture airs out, and the joining of the flesh above approaches;
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	then bind it more tightly than before, and increase his food, as I have said before; 
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	and if you see the place drying more than it should, know that nourishment cannot get there;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	then moisten it with lukewarm water, every time you unbind it, and this should be every third day, and loosen the bandage a little; 
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	by this method, then, nourishment flows to the limb, and quickly corrects what foolish physicians do, who improperly set the limb:
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	this is bad, and also frightening work, and I see nothing else to do but to leave it alone and work on it correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of the different types of fractures
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many kinds of fractures, and various forms, and the causes are distinct;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	for there are fractures caused by the blow of a sword, and the neck of the bone cuts the entire bone down to the syfac which is underneath the bone, as an axe does with wood;
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	and this type of fracture is called a "hatchet fracture".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	Or the sword cuts the bone from above without piercing, and this type of fracture is called "complete";
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	and the wound of these two fractures is large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a blunt percussion, or a split or a cut from a stone, or from falling on a stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a piercing fracture, which reaches down to the membrane that is under the bone, or it is on the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And also a wound which is placed in the bone as thin as a hair, and the crack is small, and therefore this fracture is called "hairline";
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	and if the wound, which is made either by striking with a stone, or by falling, or by a similar thing, causes the piece of bone to go down, and the place is sunken in as do the cauldron makers when they strike the cauldrons;
si entre li piere dedens.	then the stone enters inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more often to those who have moist bones in their head, like a child's head;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and it happens in all these types of fractures that small pieces are separated like splinters;
et je em parlerai en son leu.	and I will speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all kinds of fractures by the depression above them, and probing with a tent, and by the corrupted flesh which is on top.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hairline fracture is recognized because when the bone is uncovered, and one rubs ink on it, the fracture appears black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, pay attention to the patient's symptoms, and if you see any bad symptoms, such as vomiting bile, and loss of consciousness, and stretching, and swelling, and high fever, and the eyes bulging and red, and other similar symptoms with many variations, then it certainly cannot heal.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see alarming symptoms, and you hope for recovery, then begin treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wounded person first comes to you, and it is in winter, it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day as quickly as you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, before the tissue under the bone becomes corrupted, and the symptoms we have mentioned appear.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the fracture of the bone reaches the membrane that covers the brain, then you must cut the fractured part thus:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	And you should take the head of the wounded patient, and uncover the bone in all the ways you can, and over the shape of the wound as gently as you can, and if bleeding occurs when uncovering the bone, or a hot abscess, treat it appropriately, and then fill the area with cloths soaked in rose oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	And let the wound rest until the hot abscess is calmed, and you are sure of the cessation of bleeding;
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	Then begin to remove the bone around the edges, and this is done according to two methods of operation:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	One method is that you cut with a narrow chisel in front, and this is the shape:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then use another chisel larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second method is that you have a number of different chisels, some narrow and others wide, and they should be pointed, and made of Indian steel;
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and work lightly, so that you do not injure the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is strong and hard, then you must pierce around it, before you use chisels with drills, not so deep that they pierce through the bone of the skull, and it should have on the tip a flange or a circle, so as not to let the point pass through the bone;
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	and you must have several of them, so that each one comes in its place according to the thickness of the bone, so that you have drills for every skull;
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	and this is the form of the three types of drills:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The method for piercing around the fractured bone is that you place a drill on the bone, and turn it with your fingers until you know that the bone is pierced;
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	then put the drill somewhere else a little further on, and so do all around, then cut with chisels the piece of bone which is between the holes, and do this as carefully and lightly as you can, as we have said, until you remove the bone with your hand, or with some of the instruments that you have, such as tongs, forceps;
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	and be careful not to touch the brain or the dura mater.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and extracted the bone, you must cut the piece that remains of the bone with another instrument similar to a chisel, but it must be thinner and more delicate than the other chisel;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	and if any small bones or splinters remain, remove them gently with one of the instruments;
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	then treat the wound with dressings and ointments that we have mentioned.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And the other method of operation is the one that Galen described, which is safer;
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and he praises it highly, and these are his words.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	You must first expose a part of the bone, there where the fracture appears most obvious, so that when you have exposed that part, you will place under the head of this lenticular incisor, of which this is the shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut on one side, and the part is sharp on both sides, so that the cutting edge is towards the bone;
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	then strike with a small mallet, so that you lightly cut the bone all around, and take good care of the membrane that is underneath;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it is attached to the bone, remove it lightly, for it can be removed well without harm, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not penetrate to the membrane, and the bone is only cut on the surface, and there are small pieces, then it is necessary to smooth this roughness, and remove the splinters with a fine scraper of which you should have various sizes, to administer in each place the most suitable one, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	So start again with large scrapers, and then with finer ones, and do not stop doing this until it is good.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	In each of the other hair-line cuts and fine fractures, you must administer treatment according to its correction;
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	and this is something that is not entrusted to one who has not applied himself to the study of this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the peritoneum is exposed, you must take a linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and soak it in rose oil, and place it on the wound;
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	then take another cloth, folded in two or three, and soak it in wine and rose oil, and place it over the first cloth;
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	and do this as gently as you can, so as not to aggravate the peritoneum, then apply another bandage over it, and do not tighten it except enough to hold the wound covering in place; 
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	and leave it like this for a day or two, until the hot inflammation has subsided, then untie it and apply medications such as lily roots, and vetch flour, and incense powder, and birthwort, and similar things;
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and make a powder of these things, and put it on the wound, and constantly apply cleansing medications without causticity;
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	and make sure the wound is always clean, that you do not leave the ointment there, and do not allow pus to collect, because when pus collects on the wound dressing, it will rot and become infected, and this will cause the patient great harm;
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	because when you put something caustic on the peritoneum, it blackens on the surface.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, take heed, if any bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, it is undoubtedly doubtful.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if blackness appears only because of the medicine that has been applied, which has such a property, then you must take one part honey, and three parts rose oil and a drop of glue, and put it on the peritoneum;
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with the appropriate treatments, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Know that sometimes both parts of the nose above are broken, or just one of them, for there are two bones;
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	and the one below is cartilaginous, and does not break, but only bends or twists, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, you must insert your little finger into the nostril, and align the fracture inside with your index finger and thumb from the outside, until the nose returns to its natural shape; 
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do this gently, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the nose, and the finger cannot reach the spot, then you must align it using the end of a somewhat thick rod. 
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is in two parts, do the same, and hurry to restore it the first day, if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the hot swelling has subsided, then insert linen cloth tents into the end of the nose, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	Or insert another one on the other side, if the break is there;
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	and the tents should be so thick that they fill the holes of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some restorers say that the tents should be moistened with butter and changed every day. 
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	It does not seem good to me, but they should be moistened in a mixture of egg white and powder of wheat flour;
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	then leave the tent until the bone is firm and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And sometimes goose feathers are placed in the nose instead of tents, and a soft cloth is wrapped around it, and the fracture is held, and the patient breathes through it;
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	now do whatever you wish.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if hot abscesses appear in the nose while you are working there, apply cerate or cotton moistened with rose oil, or a little diachylon.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if hot abscesses do not appear there, apply a soothing plaster of sesame flour and incense powder, mixed with egg white, then place light compresses on top, and do not tie the nose;
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the nasal fracture is small, and it is broken into small pieces, extract them with suitable instruments, then sew up the wound, and treat it with flesh-generating and healing things, such as suitable plasters and ointments;
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no wound inside the nose, treat it with tents, and put lead tubes in it until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the fracture of the mandible/jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible/jaw is broken underneath, and there is no external wound, and the fracture is internal only, and is not broken in two, except for internal fragments, it is easily recognized.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is necessary, if the fracture is on the right side, that you put your index finger in the patient's mouth;
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	And if the fracture is in the left mandible/jaw, put your right index finger in, and gently push the fracture inwards, and adjust it with the other hand from the outside, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the mandible/jaw is separated in two, then you must apply traction from both sides until it is even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if loosening or breaking of the teeth occurs, secure them with a gold or silver or silk thread, then apply a plaster to the broken mandible/jaw, and put on a double bandage;
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And put over the bandage a well-made large splint, or a piece of leather evenly shaped, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it on as tightly as you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the shape changes, untie it on the third day, and then reset what has changed;
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	and apply a plaster, made from mill dust with plenty of egg or sesame flour, after you have removed the previous plaster;
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	and put light wool over the plaster, and if the plaster dries and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until he is healed;
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	often he is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if hot abscesses develop, then administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is a fracture and a wound together, see if any piece of bone has been removed;
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	then carefully remove it with instruments suitable for this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with a lancet according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and none remain, stitch the wound, if it is large, and apply one of the plasters suitable for this, to generate flesh, until it is healed.
de la forcele	Of the forceps/tweezers
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The forceps often break forward, towards the shoulder, and the breakage occurs in three ways:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	or it is broken and separated in two, and there are pieces, and it is the easiest to restore;
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	or there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the procedure is as follows when the fracture is without a wound: you should have two assistants, so that one holds the shoulder where the forceps/clavicle is broken;
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the other extends the neck towards the side;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	then set the fracture evenly with your fingers, so that the shape is as it should be, and there is neither a bump nor a depression.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you need to extend it further, place a round bolster made of cloth, or wool, under the patient's shoulder, and its thickness should be according to your need;
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	and extend and lift the clavicle, and press down on the bolster with your hand, so that you evenly set the fracture, as is necessary.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the end of the clavicle outwards, because it goes inwards too deeply, then the patient must lie often on his back, and place a medium-sized pillow under the shoulder, and the practitioner pushes the shoulder down, until the bone of the clavicle is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	And then straighten the fracture with your fingers, and if you find it shattered, then you must cut into it;
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and gently pull out the pieces, and if the bone cannot be joined because of some overlapping, then trim it with one of the incisors that you have;
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but you should place this instrument under the clavicle, to protect the periosteum:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and it resembles a spoon, and is not sharp, and is as wide as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the requirements of the work;
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and it has two heads, as you see, and one is wide, and the other is narrow, like the shape of the wound that you made when you pulled out the bones;
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are sure of a hot abscess, then stitch the wound, and if the opening is small, or you suspect a hot abscess, then fill the wound with compresses and tents, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot abscesses develop there, soak a cloth in rose oil and vinegar and wine, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The tightening of the bone, when it is without wounds and without incision, is that you put on the bone a plaster of mill dust and egg white, and put light padding on it, and put a splint under the armpit, if you need it;
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	then take a very large bandage, a palm wide, then put a doubled cloth over the padding and the plaster;
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	then take a thin splint three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage so that the ends of the bandage hang down;
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	and place the splint over the fracture, and turn the bandage over the neck and under the healthy armpit, and under the injured armpit;
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and bring it around from each side, and when you see that the bandaging holds the fracture properly, and you clearly see that the splint does not move on the broken bone, then check it every day, and when the bandaging loosens, tighten it;
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	and have the patient lie on his back, and when he sleeps, put a small pillow under his armpit to raise the shoulder up;
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	this will relieve the pressure on the fracture by easing the shoulder, or you can tie his arm to his neck and not untie it unless some bad incident occurs, until twenty days have passed;
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	then reapply the plaster, if you see that there is need for it, and tighten it and leave it thus, until he is recovered;
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	and it is restored in most cases within twenty-eight days, and in some men, sooner.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the fracture of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	It rarely happens that the shoulder breaks except in a wide place or in the middle, and one does not know it except by touch;
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	so prepare it according to the form of the break, and restore it according to its natural form, in every way that you can;
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	then put on the area mill dust with plenty of egg, and light stuffing, and put on a double cloth;
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	then put on a wide and thin splint, a little wider than the shoulder, and if under the splint there are hollows in any place on the shoulder, fill that hollow with linen stuffing, so that the splint sits evenly;
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	and then bind it all firmly with a large bandage, so that the splint does not move from its place, and check the bandage every day;
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	and every time it loosens, tighten it, and adjust the splint if it is out of place, and have the patient lie on their side;
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	and the shoulder is restored in twenty days or in twenty-five.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when this time is complete, unbind it, and be certain, for it is not a bone that dislocates easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone protrudes forward, and points below the heart, then cut over it, and remove it, and do what we have said regarding the breaking of the clavicle to soothe a hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the breastbone/sternum
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The breastbone/sternum is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely;
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but it often breaks lower down.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it sinks downwards, and the patient feels great pain, and shortness of breath, and coughs, and perhaps vomits blood, and the displacement is visible in the broken bone, and one can feel it well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration is as follows: the patient often lies on his back, and you place a cushion between the shoulder blades, then press the shoulders, and bring the ribs of the two sides together with your hands, and be careful to set it evenly in all the ways that you can, so that the shape of the bone is as it should be;
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	then apply plasters and compresses on a thin splint of wood, or other light wood, and wrap it in a cloth, and tie it over the broken bone, so that it does not move;
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	and wrap the bandage around the back, and tighten it appropriately, and check the bandage every hour, and if it loosens, tighten it;
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	and if it needs to be untied, because of corrosion or itching that occurs at the site, or pain or abscess, then hurry, and untie it, and scrape the plaster, and address what has appeared there by means of treatments;
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	then reapply the plaster, and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the fracture of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	Know that the fracture of the ribs only occurs in thick places near the back, and at the end inside, and they only bend because they are slippery;
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	and one feels it well by examination with the fingers.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is that you set the fracture evenly, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, and bind it with a splint, if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the rib fracture is pointing inwards, the patient feels very great pain, and a pricking sensation, like pleurisy, because the bone pricks the membrane;
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	and breathes with difficulty, and coughs and vomits a large amount of blood, and this is a serious condition, and the ancients have put much effort into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And there are some who say that it is necessary to administer foods that swell the belly, to push the fracture outwards.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, so that hot abscesses do not develop there, if they have not already appeared.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have appeared, then treat them.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And some of them said that one should place cupping glasses on the area, to suck strongly, and this seems reasonable;
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	however, there is concern that the cupping glass may attract excess fluids to the area due to its weakened state.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some of them said that the area should be covered with wool soaked in hot oil, and tents should be placed between the ribs to make the place even all around, then it should be treated with the treatment for pleurisy, with food and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot bear from the bone piercing the skin, and there is concern for the patient, then it is necessary to cut over the location of the broken rib, and it is necessary to place an instrument underneath to protect the peritoneum;
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then one should cut the bone, and pull gently, and then sew the two edges of the wound, if it is large, and treat it with plasters, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if hot abscesses develop, then apply cloths soaked in rose oil, and place them on the area;
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and meanwhile treat the area as appropriate for an abscess, and let him lie often on the side where he should, until he is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the fracture of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	Sometimes a fracture occurs in the bones of the neck, and rarely does it bend;
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, take note if you see their hands softened and swollen and dead, and they cannot move or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that he is mortally [injured] in many cases, and if he moves them and feels well when they are squeezed and pricked, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured, if care is applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if a similar thing occurs in the spine of the back, and you want to know if he will be healed or not, note if the feet are softened, and if the same symptoms are there as in the hands, and on the back jumping flatulence and involuntary defecation;
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	and when he is turned on his stomach, involuntary defecation occurs.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is turned on his back and he wants to sit up, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	Know that he is mortally wounded:
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	so do not work on his treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen to him, then the matter is less serious.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the treatment is that you look to see if there is a hot abscess, then put on the spine rose oil or oil of egg yolks, until it is soothed;
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	then apply one of the strengthening and drying plasters, and bind it with a bandage, and tell the patient to rest;
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	and not to sleep on the side where he feels the pain, until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	And if any bone is separated, then it is necessary to cut to the heart; 
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and remove the bone, then bring together the two edges of the wound, if it is large, with a suture, then treat it with flesh-generating ointment until it is healed;
