et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "tail head," then place the ball of your left hand there and align it with your other hand as best you can, then apply the plaster and splint, if you need it;
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then bind it, and if there is a separated bone, then cut open, and remove it, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	It rarely happens that the hip bone is broken, and if it happens, it only happens with a small fragmentation at the head;
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	and cut lengthwise, and lean towards the inside, and the patient feels pain in the area, and a pricking sensation, and swells up where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And the restoration is such that you extend your hand over it, until you are over the fracture;
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	and you know what the fracture is and its shape;
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	and if the fracture is only at the head, then make this fracture even, so that it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is lengthwise, or it leans inwards, then have the patient lie on their stomach, so that the resetting of this fracture is prepared for you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	And when you have set it evenly, then apply the plaster, then put on a splint of wood or leather, and tighten the fracture, so that it does not move;
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	and pad the place below the ribs, so that the bandage is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side, or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	And if a hot abscess develops there, do not touch it until the hot abscess has subsided, and apply what we have said before;
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	and then return to the restoration, and tighten it as needed, if there is no adverse event;
et c’est li maniere.	and this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the fracture of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The shoulder blade is that which is between the neck and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, it should be restored according to one of the two methods:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	one of which is that you take a stick of medium thickness, of this shape:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	And tie two cords to the two ends, and hang them up, and have the patient sit on a seat;
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	then place their broken arm on the stick, up to the armpit, and have a curved piece of wood in the middle, then hang some heavy object on it or have the assistant extend it downwards;
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	then the physician sets the fracture by putting his hands together, until the fracture returns to its proper place.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that you lay the patient on their back, and tie their hand to their neck, then instruct two assistants, one to hold above the fracture with his hands, and the other to hold below with a cord, and each pulls on their side.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you want the pulling to be stronger, tie a cord below the fracture, and above the fracture, and have each assistant pull on their side.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the fracture is close to the head of the shoulder, you should place a cord under the armpit, and another towards the neck, below the fracture;
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	and similarly if the fracture is near the neck, a cord must be placed there gently, without force, so that the fracture is aligned with the place, and with the neck;
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	then set the fracture properly, as it should be, and bind it, unless an abscess develops there.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if an abscess develops there, do not bind it for up to seven days, and apply wool soaked in vinegar and rose oil, until the hot abscess subsides; 
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	then bind it, and the way to bind it is to put the plaster on the fracture, then bring the arm against the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the chest;
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	and put on the bandage, and tighten it over the shoulder and over the arm, so that the arm is in the shape of a star, unless something prevents it, or if the bone is displaced.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you are concerned that the bone might move, use splints, and place a splint on the fracture wider and stronger than the others, and have a finger's width of space between each splint, and each splint should be large enough to extend three fingers' width past the fracture on each side;
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	then bind over the splints, as I said at the beginning of the chapter on the fracture, tighter and less loosely.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if you consider the placement of the splints, and the bandaging, as we have described, at the time you are setting the broken limb, and you fear a hot abscess, leave it unbound until the seventh day, as we have said; 
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	then check the bandaging every three days, so that itching or swelling does not occur at the location, or that nourishment cannot reach the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	Adjust it, as we have described.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	And if no such issue arises, do not unbind it before three days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back, with his hands on his stomach;
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	and place a cushion filled evenly with wool under the shoulder, and check every hour of the day or night that the alignment of the broken limb does not shift, or that the bandaging does not loosen;
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	correct it with the power of medicine, and give him the food that we have mentioned before, in such a way that the food is initially light;
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	and when he begins to recover, let it be substantial.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	And it is customary that the shoulder and the leg should be fully healed in forty days;
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	and then it should be untied and administered a bath and medicinal ointments to restore the area.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the stiffness is severe and swollen, it takes fifty days or two months to loosen.
de la brisure du bras	of the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the two "radius" bones, of which one is small, and this is the one that follows the thumb;
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	and the other is large, and is the one that is below, towards the little finger;
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	perhaps the large radius bone is broken alone, or the small one, and perhaps both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	When the small radius bone is broken, the restoration is easy, and the healing;
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	and when the large one is broken, the healing is bad, and more serious than when they are both broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small radius bone that is broken alone, it should be extended a little, lightly, and set evenly.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	And if it is the large radius bone, it must be extended more strongly;
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	and extend it on a cushion, and hold the ball of the hand higher than the rest, and the little finger lower than the other fingers, and let the patient be propped up on himself, with a cushion in front of him, higher up, so that the patient doesn't suffer any strain;
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	then let the practitioner extend his arm on the underside of his hand, or with a cord, and another practitioner on the other side above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then let the physician set it evenly, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if there are pieces in the fracture, put each one in its place, and if there is any separated that pricks the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then cut open and remove it, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	And if there is a wound with the fracture, I have spoken of it in the individual chapter;
si pren la cure.	then undertake the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	And if at the beginning of the restoration hot abscesses arise, then glue on a cloth of cerate made with rose oil and white wax, that is neither too hard nor too soft; 
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	and tie a cloth over it delicately, until the hot abscess is soothed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	And then remove the cerate, and apply a poultice of mill dust with plenty of egg, then apply the splints, and the splint for the fracture should always be stronger, and a little wider than the others;
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	and know that there should be six splints on the arm in several positions:
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	whether the fracture is in one of the bones, or in two;
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	and tighten more over the fracture than elsewhere, and always less as you move away, as I said at the beginning of the chapter;
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	and the bandages that are over the fracture should be soft and moist, and not hard or rough;
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	and the thread with which it is tied should be linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And examine the limb and the bandage after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	And if any adverse event occurs to the limb, such as itching, then you must bathe the limb with warm water, until the itching is soothed;
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	and let the limb rest, not tightly bound.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then resume the bandaging, and if the bandage is loose and the bone separated, or similar thing, then adjust it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And take care if nourishment cannot reach the limb, because it is too tight, then you must loosen it a little, and leave it thus for a few days, until the nourishment flows there, and then tighten it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said happen to the patient, do not unbind it for up to twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	or thereabouts, then he hangs his hands around his neck, and his neck should be straight, and he should avoid movement and restlessness, and sleep on his back;
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	and know that this fracture is restored in thirty days or in thirty-five, and perhaps in twenty days, depending on the compositions and complexions of the humors.
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and at the knuckles of the fingers, few fractures occur, and there is often only swelling.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	And when the palm of the hand is fractured or bent, it is necessary that the patient sits cross-legged, and sits straight before him evenly; 
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	then he places his hand on your outstretched thigh, and the practitioner extends the broken bones, and sets them evenly, until they are well joined;
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	and applies the plaster and the padding, if no abscess develops, then applies a splint according to the size of the area;
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	and it should be wrapped in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if the fracture is on the inside around the hollow of the palm, make a ball of cloths, and instruct the patient to squeeze it against his fractured palm;
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	and then bind it with a long cloth, and let the splint be of soft leather, as large as the palm of the hand, and bind it as needed.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is on the outside, you must put a splint on top and another underneath in the palm, so that the hand is open and straight, then tie it all around the hand, and tighten the bond between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	And if the fracture occurs at a knuckle of the fingers, if it is the thumb, set it evenly, as needed;
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	and bind it with the palm, and if you see fit, put a small straight splint to raise the fracture, so it does not move;
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	and if the fracture is in the other fingers, such as the index or one of the others, align it, and tie it with the healthy finger next to it;
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	or you tie them all together in one grip, which is better, or you put on a splint, as with the thumb;
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	and take care in the restoration and in the treatment of a hot abscess, and help those it affects, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The thigh bone is often broken, and it is clearly visible when it turns forward and backward;
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	and the restoration is such that one ties one bandage above the break, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	And the patient lies on his face, then each attendant extends his bandage on his side equally;
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	and this is when the break is in the middle of the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is near the top of the thigh, let one of the bandages be towards the buttock, and the other bandage below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	And also if it is near the knee, then let the bandage be next to the knee, and the extension be downwards;
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	then the physician sets the bone straight with his two hands, until it is in its natural shape, and then applies the plaster, and bandages it, if no abscess develops.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	And if there is a hot abscess, let it subside then return to your work and your treatment;
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	The binding is done in this way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	You must wrap a hard bandage, doubled in two or three, over the fracture, leaving the excess, then bend the leg so that the heel comes to the base of the buttock, and place a long thread between the thigh and the leg, next to the knee underneath, and bring the ends of the thread to the top;
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	then turn the bandage over the leg and the thigh, then place splints on the fracture, and place a splint on the leg bone;
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	then fill the empty space between the leg and the thigh with soft cloths to even out the pressure, then begin to tie tightly three or four turns over the fracture;
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	and the higher you go above the fracture, the less you tighten it;
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	then pull on the two ends of the thread that you placed between the leg and the thigh, and tie the three splints that are on top, then go back down to the end of the thread, until you come near the foot;
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	and tighten it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like that, until no abscess, swelling, or other similar thing appears.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	And if it does occur, untie it, and address what appears there, as we have said many times;
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	and if there are pieces of bone that stick out, you must remove them, if possible;
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	and if not, then it is necessary to cut into the area and pull them out;
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	And sometimes the thigh is broken so that splints are put on it, just as with the shoulder and the arm;
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	however, in a restoration done this way, the patient does not limp.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thigh is restored in fifty days, or a little less or a little more, according to the differences in complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the kneecap
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the kneecap, fractures rarely occur, but it bends often.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is only a fissure, or a hole, and it happens with a wound, and without a wound, and this one feels well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	And the restoration is that one sets even that which is round with one's fingers, as much as it can be assembled by feel;
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	then apply the plaster, and put a round splint, if you need one, and tighten it as needed, then consider all the dispositions that we have discussed in other fractures, such as hot abscesses and other similar things;
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	so apply to each injury what is appropriate, until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is rightly called "fibula," and the other is called "tibia";
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	and fractures occur just as they do in the arm, and therefore the restoration is similar to that of the arm, and the procedure is the same. And if both bones are broken together, then the leg turns in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the slender bone is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	And if the large bone is broken, there is great pain, and it is clearly visible;
et torne desoz.	and it turns downwards.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	Then apply traction, and set it evenly, and bind the splints evenly as well;
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	but nevertheless, if the fracture is severe, and there are many pieces, the traction must be less and lighter;
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	and align it according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	And when you have completed all your work, then take two wooden splints, shaped so that they enclose the leg on one side and the other, and are the length of the leg from the knee to below;
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	then wrap in two places a bandage above and below, and tie it in the middle also, and at this point the leg will not be able to bend to the right or left, and so it is well;
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	and some apply a cradle the length of the leg, and it is made of wood, and the leg is placed in it to prevent movement, and this is properly done in a fracture where there is a wound;
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	and move the leg each day to see if there is a hot abscess or another problem;
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	thus treat it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no fracture, but in the bones of the foot sometimes there is a fracture and in the toes a little, and there rarely occurs more than a simple fracture in several places.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	And if there is a fracture in the bones of the foot, and you see these bones overlapping each other, have the patient put his foot on the ground, as if he wanted to walk, and then immediately put your foot on his, where the bones are raised, then press it until they return to their places;
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	then put the plaster and padding on it, and place under the arch of the foot a small board with two flat ends, then tie it to the leg appropriately, after you have wrapped cloths around it, and other things that you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, untie the bandage, for you will find the bones even, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	And if any of the toes are broken, set them as we have described for the fingers of the hand;
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	then put on the broken toe a splint along the length of the toe, and let it be a little wider, then place under the foot that board which I mentioned, and tie it appropriately;
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	and if there are two or three, or more, broken, put on each toe a splint according to its size, wrapped in a linen cloth, and tie the board under the foot;
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	and it should extend over the end of the board beyond the arch of the foot, so that it holds it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	And you must not forget the other things that I have mentioned for other fractures, from what we have said;
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	and treat each incident as appropriate.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the wrist bone
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	When the bone of a woman's hip is broken, have her sit spread-legged, then lean her back, and be held from behind;
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	then the practitioner fills the patient's vagina with cotton, and puts in as much as a fist;
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	then have the woman stand, and lift her back little by little, and then the cotton jumps out, until it comes to the opening of the vagina, and the bone returns with the wad;
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	and when she needs to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back, and do this for seven days or thereabouts:
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	thus the fracture will be restored, and if you wish, take a sheep's bladder, and tie a tube to the opening, and put the whole bladder into the vagina;
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	then blow strongly into the tube, until the bladder is inflated inside:
la nature si revenra li brisure;	the vagina will return to its place, the fracture; 
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then it should be filled with cotton, and left like that for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	And when the wrist bone of a man, or of a woman, is broken, restore it as we have described for the hip bone;
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	and these fractures, close together, are not hidden from him who applies his study and practice, and understands my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	For the fracture itself, in many arrangements, indicates the right way to restore it:
enten le donques.	understand it then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	For the penis, when it is broken, take a goose quill and place the penis inside;
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	then wrap cloths around it, and leave it for three days or thereabouts, and it will be quickly healed.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with a wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with a wound, especially if it is large, such as in the bone of the thigh or shoulder or similar, that it be healed immediately, as the healings that we have described demonstrate.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, staunch it with vitriol if you have nothing else, then begin to restore the fracture in that same hour, or that day, if hot abscesses do not arise.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if hot abscesses arise, leave the restoration until the ninth day, until the abscesses are calmed, and do not touch them on the third or fourth day, for you would cause a bad outcome.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is apparent on the open flesh, then you must set it lightly with your hands, using slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	And if the extension devices are not ready for you to use with your hands, then set it with this instrument which is made of iron, which is seven or eight fingers long, and its width is according to the size of the wound;
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	and for this reason the physician needs to obtain three or four, according to what he needs for each treatment of a fracture;
et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	and it should be round and a little thick, so that it does not bend under the pressure on the limb during your work, and it should be pointed at the front, and thicker from the middle forward, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	And it is called "lever," because the curved end must be placed on the end of the exposed bone;
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	and push it at once, until it returns, and is aligned with the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is fine, and the instrument cannot grip the bone well, then you must trim the end of the bone, so that the instrument can have a hold on it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	And if you cannot reduce the bone, as we have said, then cut it with a suitable instrument, either an incisor or a saw, as you are able; 
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	then smooth what remains of the bone's roughness and small splinters.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is set, and the patient feels great pain afterward, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	So work until it is in its place, then soak a cloth in dark, astringent wine, and especially if it is in summer; 
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	and do not put on the wound a cerate or anything else containing oil, lest it cause rot and corruption;
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	then apply splints once you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and fit the covering all around, according to the size of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not constricted by the bandage; 
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	and many times foolish physicians have done this, and have caused the patient to die or sometimes to become crippled;
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	and the bandaging should be softer and gentler than other bandages.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	And if the wound is bad or large, and you fear that a bad outcome might occur, as we have said, and you find pain at the location, then you should not apply splints;
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	but wrap around, instead of splints, hard cloths, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days pus forming at the wound, then remove what you have put on with wine, and apply a wound-healing ointment, such as tetrapharmacum ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you must unbind the limb twice a day, morning and evening, until it is healed and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And the limb must be positioned in such a way that the pus flows downwards easily.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if many days pass, and it cannot heal but continually produces pus, know that there are small pieces of bone, for which you must explore the wound with a probe, and remove all these separated pieces which cause this pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula develops at the site, or another kind of infection, you must treat it according to what is said in its chapter earlier.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	And when the bone is broken, and exposed on the limb, like the bone of the thigh or the shoulder, and other similar large limbs, do not pull on it, because death often results, but leave it until it rots;
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	perhaps it will fall off by itself after 20 or 30 days, then treat the wound, if you can;
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	and if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of burns that come upon a burn scar/scab
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	We often see, after the healing of a fracture, especially when it is near a joint, an ugly thing to see, the shape of the limb;
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	and perhaps the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	Therefore, take care if the knot is fresh:
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	then administer styptic medicines, such as aloe, frankincense, and myrrh, and sarcocolla, acacia, and similar others, so that you take some of these, or all together, and mix them with styptic wine or with egg white or with vinegar;
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	and put them on the knot at night in compresses, and tighten it well, and do not loosen it for many days;
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	and then undo it, and start another one, until the nodule is removed;
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	or you tighten over it a well-made piece of lead;
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	for the property of lead is that it removes all swellings from the limbs;
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	and if the nodule has already turned into a hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then cut over it, and incise the apparent excess;
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	or you scrape it with a scraper, until it is removed, and treat it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the limb that is weak after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	When the bone fracture is restored, and the limb remains weak and thin afterward, it happens for many reasons:
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	one of which is because it was bound too tightly, and was not bound as it should have been;
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	or because there were too many bandages, and nourishment could not reach the limb;
ou por multitude d’arosement;	or because of excessive irrigation (washing/bathing);
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	or because of too much movement, not at the right time;
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	or because he has little blood in his body, and is thus weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	And the treatment is that you make the patient eat, and make the body supple, until the blood is increased in him; 
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	and administer baths to him, and give him joy and happiness;
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	then put pitch on the limb, so that the pitch attracts great nourishment to it, and frequently bathe it with warm water, so that the nourishment flows to the limb;
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	and it returns to its natural form.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	of the crooked limb after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	When the limb is crooked after restoration, and the bone is visibly broken, and the shape of the limb is ugly, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function:
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	so do not believe the fools who say that the limb must be broken all over again, and many foolish physicians have done this in our land;
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	and this practice is condemned, and great harm comes from it, and possibly death;
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	however, if the knots and distortions are fresh, they should be bathed with hot water, in which softening herbs have been cooked, such as marshmallow leaves and roots, and melilot, and similar things;
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	and make a softening plaster, such as a well-made diachylon, and take marshmallow mucilage, and mix it with chicken fat or sesame oil, and make a plaster on top;
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	or take ripe figs, and crush them with dove droppings, and similar medicines that reduce swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the knot is removed by rubbing continuously and for a long time with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And movement should be applied to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	And if the crookedness is old and hardened, like stone, and it is necessary to remove it with an instrument, then it must be cut down to the bone, with a thin scalpel, gently; 
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	and put care and study into the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation is the displacement of a joint from its place, because of which it cannot move, and the limb is deformed, and the patient feels great pain and great injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When a dislocation happens to someone, it must be reduced immediately without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	For if one delays, the area swells, and perhaps it can only be put back in place with difficulty;
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	therefore it should not be moved at the time when it is swollen:
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	often it causes spasms and other pains;
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	however, when this happens, have the patient bled, then leave it alone until the swelling has subsided;
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	then bathe the limb with hot water and oil, then reset it gently, and treat each limb as the treatment comes to its place. 
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations from the head down to the feet.
des mandibules	of the mandibles (jawbones)
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	It rarely happens that both mandibles (jawbones) are dislocated, and the dislocation of both is in two ways:
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	either they are slightly out of their places, and slightly softened;
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	or they are completely dislocated, and hang towards the chest, and saliva runs from the mouth which he cannot hold, nor can he close his mouth, and he mumbles his speech with his tongue.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is minor, it returns by itself in most cases.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is complete and full, then you must reduce it quickly, and do not delay;
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	and in such a way that the assistant holds the patient's head, and the physician puts the thumb of one of his hands at the root of the jaw's dislocation inside the mouth, if the dislocation is on both sides;
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	and the other fingers of the hands should be outside, to apply even pressure;
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	and instruct the patient to relax his jaws and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the physician sets it evenly, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	And if the reduction is difficult, especially if both jaws are dislocated together, then moisten them with hot water and oil, until you can reduce them easily;
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	and do not delay the reduction, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are reduced evenly, and the patient's mouth closes well without difficulty, then apply cloths soaked in a cerate made of rose oil and wax, then bind it lightly with soft bandages;
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and the patient should sleep on their back, with their head placed between two cushions, so that they do not move it to the right or left, and do not try to chew, but take light food, until the pain is gone, and the jaws are healed;
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then they can chew what they want lightly, and not strain to open their mouth when eating and drinking, until the jaw is well healed and healthy.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jawbones cannot be reset at once, and are not returned to their places, fevers and sudden illnesses may occur, and possibly diarrhea, and perhaps vomiting pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	And when you see this, then know that it is fatal;
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	and many times the one to whom it happens dies within nine days.
de la forcelle	of the splint/sling
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The splint cannot dislocate inwards from the side of the arm and chest, but it is sometimes dislocated outwards, and one feels it clearly.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	And the restoration is such that the patient lies often on his back and extends his arms;
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	and then press the place firmly with your palm, and it will return;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	then apply the plaster and the bandage, and tighten it;
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	and the head which is towards the elbow cannot dislocate;
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	at least not easily, and if it does dislocate at any time, then put it back in its place, as we have said;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	then put on the plaster and the bandage, and tighten it, and tell the patient to rest until he is healed;
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	and in the same way the head of the shoulder is reset, when it is separated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	Know that the shoulder is dislocated only in three ways:
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	one of which is that it dislocates towards the armpit below;
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	and the second is towards the chest/breast;
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	and sometimes it dislocates upwards, and this happens rarely;
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	and it does not dislocate backwards because of the shoulder blade, and it does not dislocate inwards because of the sinews/nerves;
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	and it often dislocates downwards towards the armpit, especially in those who have little flesh, because in these it jumps out easily;
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	in those who have enough flesh, it dislocates with difficulty, and returns with difficulty.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens to some men a blow or a fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think that it is dislocated because of this. 
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	It is therefore necessary that you examine it, until you are certain;
et adonques encomence la cure.	and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And the dislocation is recognized when it is down towards the armpit, and compare the injured shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find a clear difference between them;
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	and you will find a hollow at the top of the shoulder, and under the armpit when touching the head of the shoulder, as if it were an egg;
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and the patient cannot bring their hand to their nose, nor make any movements;
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and also, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you find it clearly by touch;
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	and this type of dislocation is not difficult to reset when it is recent, or if the patient is a child.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	And the method is that the practitioner lifts the patient's hand upwards, then places their fists under the armpit, and forcefully lifts the joint upwards into place;
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	and the practitioner lifts the hand and extends it upwards, then puts it underneath;
si venra hastanment.	it will return quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	And if it does not return as we have said within a few days, then the patient should be bathed in hot water;
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	and the practitioner should administer softening and soothing ointments, such as a decoction of marshmallow, fenugreek and melilot in water, and it should be applied;
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	then the patient should lie on their back, and a pad of wool, even, neither too soft nor too hard, should be placed under the armpit, then the practitioner should place their heel on the pad and carefully lift the head of the shoulder, and pull the patient's hand;
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	and another practitioner should hold the patient's head so that it does not move downwards;
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	that shoulder will return immediately, and you see, reset it in this manner:
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	and you should have a man present who is taller than the patient;
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and he should stand upright beside him, and put his shoulder under the patient's armpit, and lift the armpit up, so that the patient hangs in the air;
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	and another practitioner should pull the patient's hand downwards towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, hang something heavy with him, and the dislocation will immediately return (to its proper place).
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	And it is also reduced in another way:
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	a long stick is driven into the ground, the top of which should be as round as a pestle, and neither too thick nor too thin;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	then it should be placed under the patient, but with soft cloths on top, and the patient lies along the length of the stick;
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	then his hand is pulled downwards strongly on the other side, and the joint will quickly return to its place;
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	and if it will not return despite all these things that we have said, then do this treatment:
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	take a firebrand two arms long and four fingers wide, which has a round end so it can be inserted deeply under the armpit, in this manner:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	then tie soft cloths over the end of the stick, so that the stick does not injure the patient, then place it under the patient's armpit;
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	and extend his arm along the stick, and tie the shoulder to the stick, and the arm at the wrist, then place the arm on a rung of a ladder of sufficient width, and his hand should be extended downwards, and let the body hang on the other side:
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	the joint will return to its place immediately.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, in whatever manner, you must put an even layer of wool under the armpit, then apply the prepared plaster of mill dust, with incense and egg white, over the whole shoulder and around, then tighten it suitably under the armpit, and turn the bandage over the plaster, and bind the hand to his neck, and let the hand remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	And he should eat little, until the limb is strengthened, for it will heal faster;
et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;	and then eat more after 5 or 7 days, and move it;
et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	and if it is firm and not soft, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come there, or for another reason, you must apply cauteries with three holes, as described above in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;	And if you do all this, and it loosens after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and he cannot lift his arm up, then know that the nerves at the top of the shoulder are cut or stretched or weakened;
et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure;	The dislocation which is near the chest, and the breasts, or behind, occurs from a push, and stretching of the hands, and there one applies another dressing;
et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing, stiffness comes to the limb, and slowness in movement, then the patient should use baths many times, until that stiffness is relieved, and returns to its former state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the elbow
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;	Know that the joint of the elbow is dislocated with difficulty, and with difficulty returns;
et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;	and it is dislocated in all directions, and especially forward and backward, and the dislocation is not hidden, for it is clearly seen and felt;
et desalue selonc chescune figure.	and dislocates according to each position.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you compare the injured elbow with the healthy one, you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is separated, and he cannot bend his arm or touch his shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener;	And you must reduce it before a hot abscess develops there, because if a hot abscess were to develop, it would be difficult to reduce;
et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier;	and perhaps it cannot be completely reduced, especially when it is at the back;
si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	it is worse than other dislocations, and more painful, and sometimes death results.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains;	And the restoration, if it is such that it can be reduced, is that you extend his hand with your two hands;
et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	and his arm should be spread, and the physician's hands placed along the side, above and below, and push the joint with his thumbs together, or at the base of his palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is at the front, it is reduced when he bends his hand with his hand, and strikes with the base of the palm the side that is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension;	And if it does not want to return to its place, then apply strong extension;
et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension;	and two assistants should extend the arm, and two assistants should hold him, so that he does not move during the extension;
puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	then turn the arm in each direction, after you have wrapped it with a double-layered cloth, long and wide;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when the physician has joined the joint with his hand, he should anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, then push the joint firmly, until it returns;
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	and when it is in place, apply a dry plaster with some egg white, and bind it firmly, and suspend the arm from the patient's neck, and leave it for some days, then untie it. 
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse;	And if the joint is firm in its place, untie the bandage and leave it;
et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis;	and if you see that the joint is not tight, reapply the plaster and the bandage, and leave it thus for some days, until it is firmly set;
puis le deslie.	then untie it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez;	And if he feels severe pain after the reduction of the joint, and it moves, bathe and rub it gently, and apply pressure until it is relieved; 
ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	or you put on the joint a greasy sheep's bladder, then leave it for a day and a night, then remove it, and have him enter the bath;
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain;	and when he sweats, rub the joint temperately, then put the bladder back on, and then enter the bath;
et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do this two or three times, until he is healed;
et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus;	and if you wish, put on warm, moist cow dung with butter, and bind it on;
si revenra a sa disposition.	it will return to its proper position.
li dislocation de la main	Dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures.	The joint of the hand dislocates, and the return is easier than other joints.
Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	However, it must be returned to its place quickly, at the very hour it is dislocated, before the area swells, or a hot abscess develops there.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the reduction is done by placing the injured hand on a table, and the practitioner extends the hand, and carefully sets it evenly, placing their palm over the appearance of the joint, and pushes until it returns to place.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu;	However, you must check if it is properly in place;
adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	then have the patient place the back of their hand on a table for the extension and reduction.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, the patient should place the back of their hand on the table, and the physician should place their hand over the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	If it returns to place now, that is good.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, bind it with soothing plasters for hot abscesses, and leave it thus without restarting.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it in place after a few days, the joint will remain crooked;
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout:	and it doesn't harm the patient except that the hand is weakened, and he cannot grip anything at all:
adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere;	then know that the nerves are cut, or the artery;
si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	so there is no other solution but to burn with a cautery next to the break, and perhaps nothing else will help.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, apply the plaster that we have mentioned, then bind it and leave it for five days, then untie it and leave it like that.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is some stiffness, then wet it with warm water, and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated in any direction, sometimes on the back of the hand or on the palm;
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	then stretch the finger, and push the dislocation with your thumbs until it returns, then support the tip of the finger, and bend it toward the part where it is disjointed;
et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor;	and leave it for two days, and then set it straight that day; 
et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut;	and at night bind it, as we have said, and unbind it during the day, and make it move, and bind it again at night;
et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do this often, until it is stable, and do the same if it is dislocated on the palm of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed;
et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	and do the same, when it is dislocated elsewhere.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	of the dislocation of the spine of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine of the back or the neck is dislocated, or if there are several dislocated, there is no cure, because death quickly takes the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I.	And the sign is that the excrement comes out involuntarily, and he cannot hold it, and often some limbs are paralyzed, either both thighs or both arms or one.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars;	And often the spine is displaced in four parts;
celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	that which is displaced to the rear is called "gibbosity": (or hunchback)
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance:	The treatment is that you look to see if the gibbosity has come from childhood:
si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	then there is no cure or healing at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And that which comes from a fall or blows or similar things, the ancients spoke of methods of treatment with grand words, where there is not much benefit in any of them;
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	but I have shortened it according to my understanding, and have fashioned instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that for the gibbosity that comes on the chest in front, there is no remedy nor health;
et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and also that which comes directly on both sides, and one cannot treat except properly that which comes on the back, as I say; 
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	and the patient should be lying on their face in a level place, and have padding beneath them so they do not injure themselves;
puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	then firmly fix a firebrand in the ground at the head, and another at the feet, and tie a cord beneath the armpits of the patient, and another at the hips, and at the knees, and at the ankles;
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons;	and two assistants hold the cords, one at the head and the other at the feet, across the two firebrands;
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and let them be firmly fixed, the firebrands as we have said, and the physician places his palms firmly on the spine until it returns to place.
